Railway and Highway Liaison Measures 27

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways, after consulting with the National Economic Council, has formulated measures for the liaison between railways and highways, which have been approved by the Executive Yuan. The original text is as follows: The highway network plan shall be drafted by the Economic Council and discussed with the Ministry of Railways; the establishment and operation of provincial, municipal, and private automobile companies, as well as the approval of transportation prices and the supervision and inspection of business operations, shall be under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Railways, and the Economic Council shall be informed at any time for record; the state-owned automobile transportation enterprises run by the Economic Council shall be informed to the Ministry of Railways at any time for record; highway engineering, highway transportation facilities, and other technical matters shall be under the jurisdiction of the Economic Council, and the Ministry of Railways shall be informed at any time for record; railway and highway intermodal transportation and business transportation surveys shall be under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Railways, and the Economic Council shall be informed at any time for record; matters related to the transportation enterprises run by the Economic Council shall be jointly negotiated by both parties. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

### Longhai Railway Wei River Temporary Bridge Washed Away by Water 29

(Xi'an) The temporary bridge on the Longhai Railway over the Wei River in Xianyang was washed away by water at 3:00 AM on the 2nd, causing significant damage to several spans of the bridge on the north bank and huge losses of materials along the river. Train service has been temporarily suspended, and passengers are crossing by boat. Repairs are expected to take a few days to restore traffic. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

Aviation Committee Initiates the Establishment of the Jiang Birthday Plane Dedication Committee; Organizational Charter Approved, Office Begins Immediately; Kong Xiangxi, He Yingqin, etc. Elected as Standing Committee Members 30

(Nanjing) To celebrate President Jiang's 50th birthday this year, central government agencies and provincial and municipal authorities, as well as military commanders and civilian groups, have initiated fundraising to purchase airplanes to be presented to the government as a memorial. However, the methods vary across regions, and the collection of funds is being handled by multiple parties. There is no dedicated agency to oversee the overall effort, making a unified approach necessary. Therefore, the Aviation Committee invited representatives from the China Aviation Association, the National Aviation Construction Commission, and responsible individuals from central government agencies to discuss the establishment of a central organization to coordinate the collection of funds, purchase of airplanes, and naming procedures. It was resolved to establish the "Jiang Gong Birthday Plane Dedication Committee" to take charge of fundraising, purchasing airplanes, and naming, etc. To build national confidence, heads of central ministries and commissions, provincial and municipal authorities, pacification commissioners, university presidents, and social celebrities were invited to serve as committee members to provide guidance and supervision, with the standing committee members assuming practical responsibility. The organizational charter and fundraising and purchasing procedures were approved, and Kong Xiangxi, He Yingqin, Weng Wenhao, Zhou Zhirou, and Wang Xiaolai were elected as standing committee members. Notifications have been sent to relevant party and government agencies for record, and the office began operations at the Lizi Society today. The organizational charter and fundraising and purchasing procedures of the committee are as follows:

Organizational Charter of the Jiang Gong Birthday Plane Dedication Committee

Article 1: The Aviation Committee, the National Aviation Construction Commission, and the China Aviation Association shall jointly organize this committee to centrally handle matters related to the national fundraising and plane dedication for President Jiang's birthday.

Article 2: The name of this committee shall be "Jiang Gong Birthday Plane Dedication Committee." The office shall be located at the Lizi Society in Nanjing.

Article 3: The number of committee members is not fixed. In addition to one responsible individual dispatched by the Aviation Committee, the National Aviation Construction Commission, and the China Aviation Association as ex officio members, heads of central ministries and commissions and responsible authorities of provinces and municipalities may also be invited to serve as committee members to demonstrate national participation in this grand event (the list of committee members shall be determined by the preparatory committee and invitations shall be sent).

Article 4: This committee shall establish a standing committee of five members, organized by the preparatory committee.

Article 5: The duties of the committee shall be to guide and supervise fundraising, purchase airplanes, and assist in naming procedures. All routine matters of the committee shall be handled by the standing committee.

Article 6: The standing committee of this committee shall establish a secretary-general, as well as general affairs, finance, and design departments, each responsible for fundraising, purchasing airplanes, and naming matters. The organizational structure shall be determined separately.

Article 7: Committee meetings of this committee shall be convened as needed. Standing committee meetings shall be convened once a week, with the date and time to be determined separately.

Article 8: All expenses of this committee shall be borne by the Aviation Committee, the National Aviation Construction Commission, and the China Aviation Association, and shall not be drawn from the plane dedication donations.

Article 9: Staff members of this committee shall be designated or transferred from personnel of the Aviation Committee, the National Aviation Construction Commission, and the China Aviation Association by the standing committee members.

Article 10: Fundraising and purchasing procedures for this committee shall be formulated separately.

Article 11: This committee shall be dissolved after the fundraising and plane dedication matters are completed.

Article 12: This charter may be amended and promulgated at any time if there are any omissions.

Fundraising and Purchasing Procedures for the Jiang Gong Birthday Plane Dedication

Committee:

All donations for the plane dedication from all sectors of the country shall be centrally collected and managed by the "Jiang Gong Birthday Plane Dedication Committee."

The military and political departments, the National Aviation Construction Commission, the China Aviation Association, the central bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications shall be the initial fundraising agencies.

Donations from the people of all provinces and cities, as well as donations from branch associations of the Aviation Association in all provinces and cities, and funds that have been approved or are being prepared by the China Aviation Association, shall be collected by the China Aviation Association and transferred to this committee; donations from civil servants of various agencies shall be collected by the National Aviation Construction Commission and transferred to this committee; donations from military agencies shall be collected by the Ministry of Military Affairs and transferred to this committee. Other direct donations may be collected by the central bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications on behalf of this committee (if donations from various provinces and cities or military and police sectors are inconvenient to remit, they may be directly deposited with the three banks).

For every 100,000 yuan collected, this committee shall purchase one airplane on behalf of the donors, and the name and naming location of the airplane may be designated by the donors or groups.

If the donation is less than 100,000 yuan, this committee shall coordinate the purchase of one airplane by several groups or purchase trainer aircraft and use them to establish manufacturing plants.

If the donation is designated for establishing an aircraft manufacturing plant, it may be declared to the collection agency or bank at the time of donation.

At the end of the donation and plane dedication, this committee shall print the names and numbers of the donating agencies, groups, and individuals into a special booklet and distribute it to the donating agencies and groups in various provinces and cities for reference. The total amount of donations and interest shall also be announced publicly.

The collection period shall be from June 1st to September 30th of this year.

All expenses related to fundraising and purchasing airplanes shall not be drawn from the donations. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

Overview of Expenditure Figures in the General Budget 32

(Nanjing) The fourth-level financial expenditure item in the national general budget for the 25th year totaled 64,515,566 yuan. The breakdown is as follows: Regular financial expenses were 64,141,844 yuan, divided into nine items:

Administrative expenses of the Ministry of Finance were 1,567,047 yuan, including the expenses of the Ministry of Finance, the special commissioner's offices in Guangdong and Sichuan, and the Xiang National Tax Revenue and Expenditure Affairs Office;

Customs expenses were 31,230,424 yuan, including the Customs Administration, the General Inspectorate of Customs, and the National Customs Tariff Commission, the Customs Vocational School, and the supervisory offices of 29 customs across the country;

Salt administration expenses were 19,773,065 yuan, including the Salt Administration, the Hedong, Liangguang, and Yunnan Transport Offices, the Jinbei Trade Bureau, the Liangguang Salt Police Anti-Smuggling Team, the anti-smuggling command in the Hedong region, the Salt Affairs Inspection General Office and its subordinate agencies, and the expenses for remitting salt tax funds;

Stamp and tobacco and alcohol affairs expenses were 5,206,127 yuan;

Consolidated tax affairs expenses were 4,032,256 yuan, including the Tax Affairs Administration and the six regional consolidated tax bureaus, the tax investigation teams, and the expenses for collecting and remitting consolidated tax funds;

Mining tax affairs expenses were 287,500 yuan;

Saltpeter and sulfur affairs expenses were 241,014 yuan;

Other financial expenses were 804,411 yuan, including the expenses of the Central Mint Review Committee, the Monetary System Research Committee, and the Financial Reorganization Committee;

The first reserve fund was 1,000,000 yuan. The temporary financial expenses were 373,722 yuan, divided into six items: (1) Expenses for financial advisors: 200,000 yuan; (2) Remittance fees and bank handling fees required for the collection of surcharges by the Maritime Customs Inspectorate: 35,500 yuan; (3) Expenses for reorganizing the Huainan salt fields and purchasing surplus saltpeter from the Koubei Mongolian Salt Bureau: 105,628 yuan; (4) Start-up costs for the tax investigation team: 10,834 yuan; (5) Expenses for the Ji Saltpeter and Sulfur Bureau: 5,040 yuan; (6) Expenses for clearing official property: 16,720 yuan. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

(Nanjing) The total expenditure on internal affairs in the national general budget for the 25th year, including regular and temporary expenses, was 8,836,520 yuan. The regular portion was 5,158,914 yuan, with 3,895,134 yuan allocated to internal subordinate agencies in the first item, 1,113,008 yuan allocated to health department subordinate agencies in the second item, 99,672 yuan allocated to the Relief Commission and its two offices in the third item, and 51,100 yuan allocated to the first reserve fund in the fourth item. The temporary portion was 3,677,606 yuan, with 3,562,964 yuan allocated to the Ministry of Internal Affairs in the first item and 114,642 yuan allocated to the Health Department in the second item. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

(Nanjing) The figures for the judicial expenditure portion of the national general budget for the 25th year are as follows: regular expenses for the Ministry of Justice and its subordinate agencies were 2,112,015 yuan, and the reserve fund was 21,000 yuan, totaling 2,133,015 yuan. The construction expenses for the Ministry of Justice's subordinate agencies were 156,888 yuan, and the judicial construction expenses for various provinces were 950,995 yuan, totaling 1,107,883 yuan. The total judicial expenditure reached 3,240,898 yuan. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

Pingyang Nankang Town Raided by Bandits 42

(Hangzhou) On the evening of the 28th, over 100 bandits suddenly arrived in Guanmei Street, Nankang Town, Pingyang, armed with over 70 guns. Because the number of able-bodied men in the town was small, they retreated to the blockhouse. The bandits then carried out widespread arson and looting. It is estimated that over 170 houses were burned down, one person was burned to death, and one person was abducted. Wealthy shops were looted, with estimated losses reaching over 200,000 yuan. (Special dispatch, 2nd)

Eight Italian Newspaper Reporters Cause Trouble, Escorted Out of Geneva; Still Plan to Report News from Suburbs 45

(Geneva) The eight Italian newspaper reporters arrested last night for obstructing Prince Umberto's attendance at the League of Nations Assembly will not be allowed to remain in Geneva during the conference. According to Swiss law, they should be severely punished for insulting foreign special representatives, or face imprisonment. However, the Swiss Federal Government has decided not to prosecute them. The Swiss authorities ordered the arrested individuals to be released from prison tonight and escorted to the Italian border tomorrow. However, the Italian Minister to Switzerland has protested, requesting that the reporters be given a reasonable period to arrange everything before being expelled, and that they be escorted to the nearest point to the Italian border. It is speculated that the eight reporters will go to Coppet to submit reports to the Italian authorities, as it is a small lakeside village ten miles from Geneva. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

(Geneva) Eight Italian journalists, after causing a disturbance at the League of Nations Assembly yesterday, have been ordered by the Swiss authorities to leave Geneva that night. The reporters immediately went to Coppet in the Canton of Vaud for a short stay. Some of them are scheduled to return to Italy today, while others will stay there to provide the Italian newspapers with news of the Assembly from Coppet after it concludes. (Havas dispatch, 2nd)

(Geneva) Eight Italian journalists, after causing a disturbance at the League of Nations Assembly yesterday, were detained in the Saint Antoine prison until 10:15 PM tonight when they were released. They were escorted to the police station by several plainclothes detectives. Nicolas, the Director of Justice of the Canton of Geneva, and Goddet, the Police Chief, were both present in the station. After briefly questioning them in the presence of the Italian Minister D'Amaro and the Italian Consul General in Geneva, Colonel Spichere, they decided to expel them from Switzerland at 10:30 PM and transport them to the border that night. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

Greece Restricts Foreign Capital Inflow 46

(Athens) After a lengthy meeting with the Governor of the National Bank and other experts, Prime Minister Metaxas decided yesterday to restrict the inflow of foreign capital, as Greece's foreign exchange reserves are dwindling, necessitating this measure. According to various newspapers, imports affected by this measure amount to approximately 700,000,000 drachmas (Greek currency). (Havas dispatch, 1st)

League of Nations Extraordinary Assembly Does Not Vote to Lift Sanctions; Eden Delivers Speech Announcing British Policy; Litvinov Advocates Military Sanctions 47

(Geneva) It is rumored that the League of Nations Assembly will not pass a resolution to lift sanctions against Italy this time. However, countries that have not lifted sanctions and wish to do so will have their intentions registered by the Sanctions Adjustment Committee. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

(Geneva) According to observers of the international situation, representatives from various countries expressed their support for the League of Nations Covenant during today's meeting, leading to a more optimistic general sentiment in Geneva. Some individuals who initially feared that the first implementation of the Covenant would fail and weaken the League of Nations are now aware that their concerns were unfounded. Furthermore, countries advocating for the maintenance of European peace have formed a united front, which is also a welcome phenomenon. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

(Geneva) French Prime Minister Léon Blum recently made a statement to the press, saying, "Before I came to Geneva, I was deeply concerned that many countries would express indifference due to the setbacks suffered by the League of Nations in handling the Italo-Ethiopian dispute. Now I know that my concerns were unfounded, and I am pleased to learn that the delegations from various countries have resolved to strengthen the authority of the League of Nations in every practical way." (Havas dispatch, 1st)

(Geneva) Delegations from various countries at the League of Nations Assembly are currently preparing a draft resolution to conclude the debate. This draft resolution, originally proposed by the French delegation, will be revised at the last minute before being submitted to the Assembly, taking into account the views of all parties to obtain the support of the majority. Its contents are likely to include two items: 1. Reaffirmation of the principles contained in Articles 10 and 16 of the League of Nations Covenant (Note: Article 10 of the Covenant concerns respecting the territorial integrity of member states, and Article 16 concerns sanctions measures); 2. Proposal to organize a committee to discuss the situation in East Africa before the regular meeting in September, as well as the note submitted by the Italian government on the 29th of last month. Furthermore, the issue of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia will also be discussed. French Foreign Minister Delbos spent half a month drafting a speech, which he will present to the Assembly on Friday to explain how the French government intends to amend the League of Nations Covenant to strengthen the League's authority. (Havas dispatch, 2nd)

(Geneva) British Foreign Secretary Eden clearly announced the British government's attitude towards the Italo-Ethiopian dispute and other issues at the League of Nations Assembly this afternoon, stating that the British government believes that the League of Nations Assembly should not recognize Italy's occupation of Abyssinia under any circumstances. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov also addressed the League of Nations Assembly today, explaining that economic sanctions alone cannot restore Abyssinia's independence, and more severe sanctions, such as military plans, are needed to achieve this goal.

League of Nations Assembly Session: British Foreign Secretary's Speech 48

Continuing Sanctions Are Truly Useless; Italy's Annexation of Abyssinia Should Not Be Recognized; League of Nations Reform to Be Discussed in September 49

Eden's speech stated: "None of you here today can have any sense of satisfaction regarding the circumstances of the League of Nations Assembly's convocation. At this moment, everyone feels grief. For the sake of the interests of all member states of the League of Nations and the League of Nations as a whole, this fact should be endured. Regarding the sanctions implemented in the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, member states of the League of Nations have jointly implemented economic and financial plans. This plan itself has not been without effect; however, the purpose for which it was hoped to be used has not been realized. The changes in the military and local situation in Abyssinia have made us reach a point where the implemented sanctions cannot reverse the situation in that country. If the British government has reason to believe that maintaining existing sanctions, or even adding other economic measures, could restore Abyssinia's position, and if other member states of the League of Nations are willing to implement them, then the British government is prepared to pursue this policy. However, the British government now feels that it absolutely cannot hold this belief. In our opinion, only military sanctions could achieve this effect. In the world situation of a month ago, I dared not believe that such military action was possible. Now, we must acknowledge reality. Continuing the sanctions implemented a month ago is truly useless. The British government also believes that this League of Nations Assembly, under no circumstances, should recognize Italy's occupation of Abyssinia. The reality of the overall situation is undergoing rapid changes, affecting our attitude towards the decisions made regarding this plan. In our judgment, this cannot change the opinion expressed by fifty member states of the League of Nations last autumn regarding Italy's actions."

"There is still a crucial question, which is the future of the League of Nations. Should we say that because we ultimately failed to create a law to overcome force, we must abandon this goal? I dare say we should not say this. Since we hold such a goal at present, our efforts must be focused on the work of reform. However, it is very clear that the lessons learned in the past few months must be utilized in practice. As for the immediate future of the League of Nations Assembly's work, the British government is ready at any time to participate in any work that the Assembly or other organs of the League of Nations decide to implement. During this gathering, it may be beneficial to exchange preliminary views on the question of the future of the League of Nations. But most importantly, each country should have the necessary time and opportunity to thoroughly consider the current issues, and delays are unavoidable. Therefore, I propose that this issue be left for discussion at the League of Nations Assembly meeting in September. The British government still believes in the principles for which the League of Nations was established." The Foreign Secretary, at the beginning of his speech, praised the solemn appeal of the Abyssinian Emperor yesterday.

Next, Litvinov spoke, saying that economic sanctions alone cannot force the Italian army to withdraw from Abyssinia and restore Abyssinia's independence. This can only be achieved with more severe sanctions, such as military sanctions. However, it is now necessary for one of several countries, in terms of its geographical location and special relationship, to assume the crucial role of military conflict before this can be discussed. But no one is willing to do so without a guarantee from other countries to provide the same cooperation. This guarantee is urgently needed now, because the aggressive will of a certain major European power has left no doubt that it is accelerating preparations to carry out aggression. Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant clearly provides the League of Nations with powerful weapons. If they can be fully utilized, they can defeat any aggression."

Mr. Massey, the Canadian High Commissioner in London, also spoke today, saying that there are very few member states of the League of Nations with the strength who are willing to take necessary coercive action, even if it results in war, to achieve the original purpose of sanctions. Mr. Massey continued to recount the circumstances under which Canada first proposed sanctions, and then said that the joint attempt by various countries to protect a weak member state of the League of Nations has failed. What could be more regrettable than this? However, at this moment, Canada seems to have no other practical way to proceed except to support the cessation of sanctions. (Reuter's report from the 1st)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Assembly continued its meeting at 4:00 PM today. The first speaker was De Wet, the representative of the Union of South Africa, who advocated maintaining the current sanctions. So far, the Union of South Africa is the first among the member states of the League of Nations to make this claim. De Wet said, "The League of Nations Assembly passed a resolution on October 10th of last year, taking collective action against Italy. At that time, all member states expressed their agreement. Our government believes that this collective action is the only effective tool for maintaining security. I hereby advocate that it should be maintained at this moment, as it is the only way to protect the nations of all countries." He then said, "The League of Nations has suffered a great loss of reputation because of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute. This does not mean that the League of Nations has failed, but rather that human beings lack the ability to fulfill their obligations." The Canadian representative, Massey, then spoke, saying that the responsibility for the Italo-Abyssinian war is clear, but at this moment, there is no other way to follow except to abolish the sanctions. In short, we have exhausted our wisdom and efforts to ensure that small member states are not subjected to aggression. This attempt has now failed."

By 6:30 PM, the chairman, Belgian Prime Minister Janson, announced the adjournment of the meeting, saying that there were still representatives from fifteen countries who had registered to speak, and that the work of the Assembly could be concluded this Friday. (Havas report from the 2nd)

(Geneva) At the League of Nations Assembly meeting this morning, Australian representative Bruce gave a speech, stating that the Australian government now feels that sanctions against Italy are of no benefit. Bruce said that the Australian government, in view of all the facts, believes that in the case of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, the purpose of sanctions has become ineffective and should be abolished. If they continue to be implemented now, they will cause disaster for the League of Nations. Since they cannot be maintained, they will inevitably succumb in a few months. Announcing their ineffectiveness today is a fair way to treat Abyssinia. Bruce also asked, "Isn't it enough that sanctions have misled the unfortunate Abyssinia?" (Reuter's report from the 2nd)

Pope Urges All Believers to Vow Not to Watch Bad Films 50

Vatican City, the Holy See: Pope Pius XI recently wrote to the American bishops, instructing them to ask all believers every year to freely agree not to watch bad films, and to establish specialized agencies in each parish, under the jurisdiction of the bishops, to identify bad films. (Havas, 2nd)

Germany Suspicious of Britain: Reply to Britain Completed 51

(Berlin) Hitler's reply to the British inquiry has actually been completed. Although it has not been published, it is reported that its contents include the following points: Reiteration of the common security of Western Europe; the difficulties in the implementation of the non-aggression pact system proposed by Germany; Germany, in view of the erratic nature of British foreign policy and its proposals to reform the League of Nations, which are difficult to grasp, is reluctant to be bound. The German newspapers are now expressing anxiety about Britain's foreign policy, and are uneasy about British Secretary of War Cooper's recent speech in Paris. The Frankfurter Zeitung published an article commenting on the overall situation, asking whether Britain always wants to obtain a three-way solution, or whether it wants to form an Anglo-French armed camp and invite Germany to join. (Reuter's report from the 1st)

(London) British, French, and Belgian cabinet members discussed the future meeting of the signatory countries of the Locarno Pact in Geneva yesterday. It is expected to be held in Brussels, Belgium, in the second half of this month. According to semi-official sources here, the British government will accept this proposal. The government also hopes that Italy can participate at that time, so that the discussion can be more practical than before. As for the main issues to be discussed at the meeting, in addition to the Rhine issue, there are three other items: the issue of Germany's continued demand for colonies; Germany's attitude towards the Free City of Danzig; Germany's attitude towards Austria. If the German government has already submitted a reply to the British questions, it will naturally be submitted for study. Otherwise, it will be necessary to formulate necessary measures to conclude the matter and put it into practice. Regarding this matter, it is reported that the British Ambassador to Germany, Phipps, has submitted a report to the government, stating that Hitler's confidant, Ribbentrop, recently gave a speech to the Berlin press, and his tone implied that he did not intend to reply to the British questions. Ribbentrop also said that if Germany cannot obtain colonies one day, then it cannot be regarded as having achieved the goal of equal rights in Europe. According to the British question, it asked Germany how it interprets the term "equal rights" and how it can be considered satisfied. Now, pondering what Ribbentrop said can at least be regarded as an indirect answer to this question of Britain. (Havas report from the 1st)

(Geneva) The Extraordinary Meeting of the Council of the League of Nations, after convening on the 26th of last month, immediately announced its adjournment. It is now scheduled to hold a closed-door meeting at 6:30 PM today to discuss the issue of the Free City of Danzig, which is included on the agenda of this meeting. It is reported that the leader of the Nazi Party branch in the city, Forster, recently published an article criticizing the High Commissioner of the League of Nations, Lester, and advocated abolishing the post of High Commissioner. Lester came here the day before yesterday and met with the Chairman of the Council, British Foreign Secretary Eden, this morning. When the Council meets this afternoon, Eden will submit a report on the situation in Danzig. (Havas report from the 2nd)

(London) Sir Barton, the British Minister to Abyssinia, has returned home from his post and has arrived in Ramsgate, Kent. He recently gave a speech to local journalists, stating that the rumors that the British Embassy in Abyssinia will be closed are untrue. During his absence, all embassy affairs will be temporarily handled by First Secretary Roberts. When asked by reporters about the current situation in Abyssinia, Barton replied, "In a word, no one knows. As for the future of Abyssinia, it can only be resolved in Europe. The land occupied by the Italian army is only a part of Abyssinia. The entire Abyssinia has neither surrendered to the Italian army nor has it been completely occupied. The so-called current situation is not yet a problem." (Havas report from the 2nd)

French Delegation Issues Statement on Relations with Italy, Explaining Points Attacked by Abyssinian Emperor 53

(Geneva) Personnel from the French delegation recently stated that the railway from Djibouti in French Somaliland to Addis Ababa, which is operated by the French, has received instructions from the French government that the company authorities have always refused to transport Italian troops and military supplies through Djibouti to the interior of Abyssinia, and it is still not allowed. As for other supplies needed by the Italian army, although they can be transported, they must be done in accordance with ordinary commercial transportation methods. As for the Rome Agreement signed between France and Italy on January 7, 1935, its main purpose was to resolve all outstanding issues between the two countries in Africa. Regarding Abyssinia, all of France's economic interests have been recognized by the 1906 Anglo-French-Italian Treaty. The Rome Agreement only reiterates this. This does not mean that France recognizes that Italy enjoys political rights in Abyssinia. Moreover, since France is a member state of the League of Nations, any action by Italy that would hinder Abyssinia's political independence and territorial integrity is naturally not something that France can agree to. It is reported that the Emperor of Abyssinia made a speech at the League of Nations Fire Conference yesterday, criticizing the French railway for allowing Italian troops to use it, so the French delegation issued this statement to clarify it. (Havas report from the 2nd)

Mechanization of Soviet Agriculture: Farmers Mostly Use Combine Harvesters 58

(TASS Moscow, June 4) A year ago, only one-fifth of the grain planting area in the Melitopol District of Ukraine used combine harvesters. This year, all the grain in the district is harvested with combine harvesters. This is one example of the mechanization of agriculture throughout the Soviet Union. The grain harvest in southern Soviet Union will soon begin, and the other parts will follow soon. This year, one-quarter of all grain in the Soviet Union will be harvested with combine harvesters. This year, 61,000 new combine harvesters will be added, greatly increasing its power. The significance of combine harvesters in agriculture is not only that they can speed up the harvest (which is of great significance in agriculture), but also that they can reduce grain loss during harvest. This sometimes increases the harvest by 20% to 25%. Therefore, the increase in grain income this year due to combine harvesters will reach millions of tons. Although the widespread use of combine harvesters in the Soviet Union is difficult to achieve overnight, it is also developing significantly year by year. As the number of combine harvesters increases year by year, the training of combine harvester drivers also improves year by year. This year, combine harvester drivers have a particularly serious task. Last year, the Stakhanovite movement showed that combine harvesters had not been fully utilized. Therefore, this year, the best drivers will increase the work efficiency of combine harvesters by two, three, or four times. This year, the level of work of combine harvesters has also greatly increased.

US Finances: Shortfall of 44 Billion Yuan, the Largest Peacetime Government Spending Shortfall; Fortunately, Revenue Is Gradually Increasing and Expenditures Are Also Decreasing 60

(Washington) The US government's fiscal year has recently ended, and its government spending shortfall has reached 4,400,000,000 yuan. This is the largest government spending shortfall in the US during peacetime. US Treasury Secretary Morgenthau gave a radio address to the nation today, announcing this number and saying that public debt now totals 33,750,000,000 yuan. This year's revenue was 4,116,000,000 yuan, and expenditures were 8,500,000,000 yuan, excluding debt repayment. If the funds required for veterans' pensions are not included, the shortfall will be reduced to 2,700,000,000 yuan. The budget plan set about two years ago was destroyed by unforeseen events. The passage of the veterans' pension bill increased government spending by 1,700,000,000 yuan. The government borrowed more than 5,000,000,000 yuan this year, but there is still 2,700,000,000 yuan in cash to cover expenses next month. The government also has important cash assets in the $2,000,000,000 US dollar exchange rate stabilization fund, which will eventually be used to repay the same amount of public debt. (Reuter's report from the 1st)

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau gave a radio address to the nation tonight, reporting on the state of the fiscal year, saying that the US government's revenue has increased, and expenditures have decreased. The national economy is thriving. He cited statistics to explain that the federal government's budget deficit and the increase in public debt were purely due to relief spending and veterans' benefits. In addition, the agricultural adjustment tax was deemed illegal, resulting in a large loss of revenue. Mr. Morgenthau continued, "Total government spending was 8,500,000,000 yuan, excluding the amount of public debt repayment. Actual revenue was 4,116,000,000 yuan, with a difference between revenue and expenditure of 4,400,000,000 yuan. Since the agricultural adjustment tax was ruled illegal, the Ministry of Finance lost 500,000,000 yuan in tax revenue, but income tax has increased by 30%, other miscellaneous taxes have increased by 20%, and tariffs have also increased by 12%. National administrative expenses totaled 3,500,000,000 yuan, of which 75,000,000 yuan was for national defense, 600,000,000 yuan was for veterans' permanent benefits, 750,000,000 yuan was for public debt interest, 500,000,000 yuan was for agricultural subsidies, and 900,000,000 yuan was for other miscellaneous expenses. Reconstruction and relief expenses totaled 3,300,000,000 yuan, of which 800,000,000 yuan was for public works, 500,000,000 yuan was for direct relief to unemployed workers, 1,250,000,000 yuan was for work relief, 500,000,000 yuan was for grain purchases, and 250,000,000 yuan was for other expenses. The most significant achievement in the past three years is that the government has reduced interest rates by about one-quarter, thereby saving 260,000,000 yuan annually. However, the facts cannot be ignored, because after the implementation of sanctions, it is still not enough to change the trend of military action. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov said that Germany is preparing to invade, so he opposes reorganizing the League of Nations by weakening the covenant, and advocates strengthening the power of the covenant. There are many people who want to make the League of Nations descend to favor the actions of aggressor countries, which is unforgivable." (National News report from the 1st)

U.S. Naval Policy: Attention to Philippine Base 61

(Washington) When asked by news reporters today whether the U.S. government plans to install 16-inch caliber guns on the two new battleships to be built, the director of U.S. naval tactics, Stanley, replied that this would be decided when the design of the two main battleships is completed, and that 16-inch caliber guns are more useful to the United States than the currently used 14-inch caliber ones. (Reuters, 1st)

(Washington) An Associated Press reporter learned today that the U.S. Navy Department is paying close attention to maintaining a naval base in the Philippines. However, the decision on this matter must be made after the Philippines becomes fully independent, which is ten years from now. Military experts have divided into two factions, for and against, regarding the maintenance of this base. The reasons given by the proponents are as follows: 1. Foreign policy, especially the Open Door Policy in China, requires a well-organized defense system in the Far East. 2. American Pacific shipping routes, aviation lines, and round-the-world routes require bases to assist the navy in exerting its protection. 3. The American base in the Philippines is very close to the British base in Singapore, so it can serve as a forward joint base for the navies of both countries in case of emergency. 4. Building a strong naval base in the southern Philippines that can accommodate a large number of battleships will control the oil, tin, vegetable oil, and other necessary war materials of the Dutch East Indies. 5. If the people of the eastern Philippines decide to become a protectorate of the United States and do not wish to be independent, a permanent base can guarantee the American position in the Philippines. The reasons given by the opponents are as follows: 1. Building a naval base in the Philippines will change America's combat plans and lengthen transportation lines. If war breaks out, maintaining these transportation lines will be difficult. Most people believe that it will be impossible to maintain this base in the event of a major war. 2. The Philippines lacks industry, so if the transportation line to the United States is cut off by the enemy, it will not be able to maintain the fleet stationed in the archipelago. 3. If the United States builds a naval base in the Philippine Islands, it must build secondary bases in Guam and other islands. This will put the base directly in opposition to the Japanese navy, with no mutually recognized demilitarized zone separating them. 4. This naval base cannot harm the enemy's commerce. Even if powerful battleships are stationed here, they will be powerless, because any enemy in Asia can use other routes to transport the most important military materials. 5. The cost of maintaining a base in the Philippines is very high. Some experts here believe that it would be better to use this funding to build closer defense works. (National Telegram, 1st)

(Washington) The U.S. Commissioner to the Philippines, Murphy, left here today for his hometown of Detroit. Prior to this, Mr. Murphy had consulted with Undersecretary of State Sayre on general issues related to the Philippines and the U.S.-Philippine business conference. Former Acting Secretary of State and newly appointed Ambassador to Italy, Phillips, was also present, so it is speculated that the discussions concerned the Far East issue and the international policy of the Philippines. At the same time, President Roosevelt will also invite Mr. Hausseman, a representative of the American business community in Manila, to the White House tomorrow to discuss Mr. Murphy's return, as Mr. Murphy may be running for governor of Michigan. (National Telegram, 1st)

President Wang Talks About the Reasons for Graduate Unemployment 73

(Nanjing) The problem of unemployment among students above the junior college level has become a major issue in recent years, arousing the attention of people across the country. According to President Wang's statement on the 1st, the Ministry of Education, in view of the past surplus of liberal arts students and the shortage of practical talents, and the abnormal development of higher education, believes that this is a major reason for graduate unemployment. In recent years, liberal arts departments have been merged and practical departments have been added. The enrollment ratio of various colleges and departments of universities has been stipulated and strictly enforced. After this reorganization and improvement, the talents cultivated can gradually adapt to the needs of the country, so the unemployment situation of graduates is not as serious as rumored. There are a total of 108 public and private junior colleges and above in the country, with approximately 8,000 graduates each year. The total number of graduates in the 22nd and 23rd years was more than 15,200, and approximately 13,000 have been employed, accounting for 87% of the total. The 2,400 unemployed account for approximately 13% of the total. And the graduates who are unemployed due to using what they did not learn, mid-career unemployment, and married female students who cannot be employed due to family relations are also included. Among them, those in the liberal arts and law departments account for three-quarters, and those in science, engineering, agriculture, and medicine account for one-tenth to two-tenths. If the number of unemployed in each department is compared with the number of graduates in that department, the liberal arts account for 22%, and the law departments account for approximately 17%, which is the highest. The engineering departments account for 3%, which is the lowest. The number of unemployed medical students accounts for only 1% of the number of graduates, which is even lower than the other two departments. Among the public and private junior colleges and above in the country, one-fifth of the schools reported no unemployed students, such as Tongji, Jiaotong University, Shanghai Medical College, Shanghai Business College, Beiyang Institute of Technology, Xiehe Medical College, and the Music Academy. Judging from this situation, the unemployment situation of graduates from junior colleges and above is not more serious than in other countries. The government has already taken various practical measures. If the country's construction industry is further expanded, the facilities of our higher education will be able to fully meet the needs of the country. (Central News Agency Telegram, 2nd)

Taiwan's Military Preparations Also Becoming Tense; Army Increased to 25,000; Railways Laying Double Tracks; Makung Port Already Blockaded; Governor-General of Taiwan to be Promoted 77

Xiamen Correspondence: Japan has decided on a "New Southern Policy," using Taiwan as a base for active southward expansion. Although it is stated on the surface that this is only for the economic development of South China and Southeast Asia, the military arrangements in Taiwan this year have also become increasingly active. The slogan is "Taiwan is the First Line of National Defense." Since March, the Taiwanese military authorities have re-demarcated the main areas and prohibited outsiders from entering restricted areas, guarded by armed military police with guns. Even local Taiwanese people are not allowed to approach within 25 yards without the permission of the authorities. Foreigners coming to Taiwan are followed closely by secret agents, similar to monitoring criminals. Photography is prohibited in some places that have not been designated as restricted areas. Military equipment has been continuously shipped from Japan to Taiwan in recent months. Some are machinery for manufacturing military equipment, and most are military equipment and supplies. It is said that from January to the present, a large number of anti-aircraft guns, field guns, machine guns, and rifles have been shipped from Japan. Iron wire mesh, camp tents, and other military supplies are even more difficult to count. On average, two transport ships arrive in Taiwan from Japan every week, all carrying these items. In the past week alone, 560 boxes of munitions have been transported, and each truck is guarded by a soldier for a day after unloading. The Taiwanese coolies who transport the goods are also unable to identify the marks on the boxes. In addition, the strength of the Taiwanese army was originally one regiment, but it has recently been proposed to add a division. This has been proposed to the Cabinet by Army Minister Terauchi. If it is realized, the Taiwanese army will have a strength of 25,000. At the end of last month, the Joint Conference of Taiwanese Chambers of Commerce resolved to petition the Cabinet to establish an army corps headquarters in Taiwan and to add a naval defense headquarters to meet the needs of national defense in "extraordinary times." At the same time, it is also planned to increase the number of the 3rd Air Wing stationed in Taiwan. The construction of the airfield began last month, with a large number of conscripted laborers. In addition, the North-South railway, which runs through Taiwan, will be re-laid with double tracks after Governor-General Nakagawa summoned specialized technical personnel for planning. Several branch lines will also be added, reaching the main coastal military areas directly. At the same time, the entire Taiwan highway network is being planned. The above plans have been drafted and will be implemented upon approval by the Cabinet. The Penghu Makung naval port fortress was entered by foreign merchant ships seeking shelter from the wind seven times between June of last year and March of this year. The navy regarded them as spies and seriously reported them. However, the court only imposed fines and released them in accordance with the Navigation Law for insufficient evidence. The navy finally believed that this was an organized international espionage activity and announced the blockade of Makung Port, abolishing the opening of Makung as a foreign commercial port and prohibiting all foreign ships from entering and leaving Makung Port, which was implemented on July 1. Although Green Makung is a naval port fortress, there is also a commercial port in the same place. Now, because foreign ships sometimes enter the naval port, the commercial port is also closed, absolutely prohibiting foreign ships from taking this route to prevent spies from peeking. The Japanese First Fleet, consisting of 40 ships and more than 10,000 officers and men, led by Commander Takahashi, entered the Keelung naval port in Taipei on the 27th of last month. At the same time, the Second Fleet, consisting of 30 ships, entered the Kaohsiung Port in Tainan. Both fleets are the main force of the Japanese Navy. They came to Taiwan from the south after a large-scale exercise in a certain area. The First Fleet came to Taiwan once in the Showa 8th year (1933), this is the second time, and the First and Second Fleets have come together for the first time. From now on, the First and Second Fleets will often come to Makung and Keelung. In addition, the Japanese fleet is currently conducting combat exercises in the waters off Taiwan, Xiamen, and Shantou. It has been two weeks since the 14th, and Nan'ao, Jianshan, and Xiamen are all within its line. The actions are very noteworthy. Also, Japan has recently been advocating strengthening the military and political organization of Taiwan and advocating that the Governor-General of Taiwan be promoted, like the current Governor-General of Korea. A general-level military officer will be appointed as the Governor-General, whose position is parallel to that of the Prime Minister, directly under the Japanese Emperor, and can directly report to the Emperor without being subordinate to the Colonial Affairs Ministry and the Cabinet. This proposal is still being disputed by the Cabinet, the Colonial Affairs Ministry, and the military. If it is realized, the current Governor-General Nakagawa will resign and the naval general Kobayashi Jizao will be the first Governor-General, facing the Korean Governor-General and army general Ugaki in the north. (July 2)

Zhang Kewu, Bandit Leader in Southern Fujian, Accepts Pacification and Reorganization; Guangdong Army in Dabu Suddenly Prohibits Transportation of Rice, Grain, and Sundries to Fujian 78

Xiamen Correspondence: Due to the changes in Guangdong and Guangxi, a tense situation has arisen between Fujian and Guangdong. Although Guangdong has increased troops along the border, it has not dared to enter Fujian territory, so although the situation is tense, it has not yet reached the stage of action. What is currently attracting more attention is the issue of bandits in southern Fujian. Although the bandits in Quanzhou, Yongchun, and Zhangzhou are taking the opportunity to move, a large number of small clowns are not enough to worry about. In fact, the strength of the Dehua Zhang Kewu and Zhang Chengfu gangs, which is the greatest and most worrying, has now been successfully recruited, and the bandit problem in southern Fujian has been largely solved. After Zhang Kewu and Zhang Chengfu withdrew from Datian, they occupied Guijin on the border of Yongchun and Dehua. The Security Office sent Zhu Lvxing, a provincial government councilor, to Dehua to recruit them. Zhu ordered Ke Jiefu, the former chief of staff of Zhang Xiongnan, to contact Zhang Kewu. Zhang expressed his sincerity in accepting pacification. Ke negotiated back and forth. On the 28th, Han Wenying, Peng Tang, Xing Guoluan, the magistrate of Dehua County, and others finally agreed to send Zhu Lvxing and Ke Jiefu, together with representatives from all walks of life in Dehua, to Houchi (20 miles from the county seat) in the bandit area to meet Zhang Kewu. The method of acceptance and compilation was agreed on the 29th: 1. The sons of Zhang Xiongnan and the wives of Zhang Chengfu and Zhang's subordinates, who were captured during the previous suppression of Zhang's troops, will be transferred to the Provincial Security Office as hostages and released after the acceptance and compilation are properly arranged. 2. Zhang Kewu, Zhang Chengfu, and Xu Feifeng's troops must gather at Xishan within ten days to await the assignment of personnel from the Security Office for review and compilation. 3. During the period when Zhang's troops are concentrated in Xishan, all troops and security regiments stationed near Xishan will be temporarily withdrawn. 4. After the review and compilation, they will be compiled into security regiments and assigned to a county near Dehua (such as Anxi, Yongchun, Nan'an, or Datian) for centralized training and will be responsible for the security of the county. 5. After the review and compilation, the Security Office will provide substantial supplies. The above five items will be implemented successively after being approved by the Standing Committee. It is also internally decided that Zhang Kewu will be the regiment commander, Zhu Lvxing will be the lieutenant colonel regiment adjutant, and Zhang Chengfu and others will be the battalion commanders. The compilation of Zhang's troops has been completed. From now on, only the review and compilation training work remains. As for the Anxi Lv Zhenshan gang, although it has 700 or 800 men, its strength is far inferior to that of Zhang's troops. They have recently disturbed Taizhou and the border of Yongchun and are being jointly suppressed by the Fifth Security Regiment. There is also news that Lv's troops will soon be recruited, but there has been no concrete negotiation. In addition, although there are many small gangs in Quanzhou, Yongchun, and Zhangzhou, they are all only dozens or hundreds of people (the most is Zhang Heshan of Nanjing with 200 people). The security regiments are able to control them. The Provincial Government commissioned She Nianci as the commander of the Bandit Suppression in Southern Fujian on the 27th. All local regiments are under his command. Mr. Yu was the original deputy director of the Security Office and is very familiar with the situation in southern Fujian. He also became familiar with various factions of the local army in southern Fujian when he recruited all the local army in the province last year. With Yu's combined suppression and pacification, it will not be difficult to quell the situation. As for Guangdong Province, there are currently four divisions, one brigade, and two regiments of the Guangdong Army in 26 counties and cities. Jiaoling, Meixian, Dabu, and Raoping are under the command of Huang Renhuan of the 1st Independent Division; Fengshun, Chaoan, and Shantou are under the command of Chen Guanghan of the Guard Brigade; Zijin, Boluo, Heyuan, and Huizhou are under the command of Huang Yanzhen of the 7th Division of the 3rd Army; the 8th Division of Huang Zhiwen; Fengshun, Punin, Jieyang, and Chaoan are under the command of Deng Longguang of the 9th Division and two newly transferred salt police regiments. The organization of the Guangdong Army is: the 1st Independent Division has two brigades, with three regiments each, for a total of six regiments; the Guard Brigade has three regiments; each division of the 3rd Army has three regiments and one supplementary regiment for a total of four regiments. Currently, there are 23 regiments of Guangdong Army troops on the border of the East River and Chaoshan. In addition, there are three divisions and a total of twelve regiments of the First Army south of Xunwu in southern Jiangxi, which are now ordered to withdraw to the border of the East River and Jiangxi. Zhang Ruigui of the Third Division has withdrawn from Xunwu to Pingyuan. Therefore, the Guangdong Army that can be stationed in the East River area totals 35 regiments. It is necessary to guard against both Fujian and Jiangxi, and only the Huang Division, Chen Brigade, Deng Division, and Zhang Ruigui's salt police, etc., a total of 19 regiments, are close to the Fujian border. The Guangdong Army is currently, except for Huang Renhuan's division and Yan Brigade's move to Wuling and Zeng Brigade's move to Dabu and Raoping, a battalion of the Guard Chen Brigade has recently taken over the defense of Huanggang, Chenghai, on the border between Guangdong and Fujian. There has been no further increase in troops on the Guangdong border. However, recently, the Guangdong Army in Dabu suddenly prohibited the transportation of rice, grain, and sundries to western Fujian, causing a rice shortage and price increase in Fengshi. The price of rice in Shanghang has risen to only 5.5 sheng per yuan. Shanghang purchased foreign rice from Chaoshan and transported it to Dabu, where it was detained by the Guangdong Army. Sundries purchased in Yongding were also detained in Lushi. The Guangdong Army has recently blockaded Lushi, because Fengshi is an important town on the Fujian border where the Han River flows into the area. Passing Fengshi is Dabu in Guangdong, and Lushi is downstream of Fengshi in Dabu. The four counties of Changting, Wuping, Shanghang, and Yongding in western Fujian are in the upper reaches of the Han River basin. The import and export of goods from the four counties all pass through the Han River, with Fengshi as the general hub, passing through Dabu in Guangdong to the Chaoshan estuary for import and export. Now that the Guangdong Army has suddenly imposed a blockade, western Fujian has been greatly affected. Merchants and residents in Hangyong County have appealed to the governments of the two counties for relief and have petitioned and negotiated with the Guangdong Army in Dabu. This matter cannot but be said to be a serious situation in the tension between Fujian and Guangdong. (July 2)

Anhui Province Intensifies Flood Control; Liu Zhenhua Schedules Periodic Inspections; Telegram Orders Preparation of Flood Prevention Materials 79

Wuhu Correspondence: The water level of the Yangtze River is rising daily, especially in the past week. The Wuhu Customs water gauge has risen to 23 feet and 5 inches on the 1st, which is several inches higher than at the same time last year. The Yangtze River liners, because the islands and beaches on both sides below Datong are submerged by water and the original channels have lost their landmarks, are mostly sailing cautiously, so that the downstream wheels will be delayed until 7:00 AM to arrive at the port, about three hours later than usual. As for the small wheels running to various inland rivers, according to the customs regulations, they must stop running when the water level reaches 25 feet to avoid flushing the embankment and affecting flood prevention. The small wheels will temporarily stop running in the first ten days of the month. At this time of high water level, flood prevention along the river has reached a critical juncture. In addition to strictly ordering the supervisors of the twelve counties, including Huaining and Wuhu, to step up their work to ensure thorough prevention, Chairman Liu Zhenhua has also scheduled to depart from Anqing by wheel on the 5th of this month, accompanied by Liu Yiyan, Director of the Construction Department, and Jiang Shihui, Director of the Water Conservancy Engineering Office, to inspect the downstream counties and supervise flood prevention. He telegraphed all the county magistrates along the river yesterday to meet him. In addition to informing them of the location to be decided temporarily by telegram, he also ordered them to quickly supervise their subordinates to prepare materials for flood control and labor, and to select dangerous areas for prevention. They must present a special report when the time comes. The Wuhu County Government, after receiving the telegram, has ordered all the dike chairmen to follow the instructions, quickly prepare flood prevention materials, and select dangerous areas for construction, without any delay. (July 1)

Songjiang: Bandit Leader Executed by Firing Squad in Punan 80

The bandit leader of Punan, Li Jinxiang, aged thirty-seven, was a native of Caojing in this county. He repeatedly formed gangs in Punan to commit murder and robbery. On October 10th of last year, he and his gang robbed a passenger bus on the Shanghai-Hangzhou highway near Yanggong Temple. On October 26th, they robbed firearms from the sentry post of Ye Shaoqing's house in Mazhen Village, causing a great sensation at the time. The provincial government ordered a strict time limit for investigation and arrest. Subsequently, he committed robberies in Jiangzhuang and other places. Finally, in April, District Security Commander Wang ordered Zhao Zanchen, the former commander of the Twelfth Security Brigade, to lead troops to Punan to suppress the bandits. They bought information and arrested Li Jinxiang at Lannidu in Pudong. Under interrogation, Li Jinxiang confessed to numerous crimes without denying anything. He was handed over to the District Security Command for a thorough interrogation. In accordance with Article 2, Paragraph 5 of the Provisional Regulations for Handling Bandits and Robbers during the Bandit Suppression Period, he was sentenced to death. The sentence was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Security Bureau, which issued Directive No. 5518, ordering execution of the sentence as ruled. After receiving the order, Commander Wang immediately identified the prisoner, paraded him through the bustling streets, and then executed him by firing squad at the small drill ground.

Wuxi Station Chief Monitored Due to Case 84

Smuggling in North China is becoming increasingly serious and has spread to the Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai) Railway area. Recently, it was suddenly discovered that Wuxi Station staff members were also involved in transporting untaxed goods. The following is a summary of the matter: Wang Xingen, a ticket checker at Wuxi Station, a native of Ningbo, is known for his social skills. Last year, he was dismissed from his position by Station Chief Li Guisheng after being found to have violated station regulations. Afterwards, Wang opened a cheap eatery near the station with Zhao Benli, who trafficked in drugs. Relying on his previous work relationship with the station staff, he actually specialized in transporting untaxed goods. In July of last year, Wang also joined forces with unscrupulous merchants from Shanghai, and his business grew daily. Recently, smuggled goods from North China have infiltrated the Jinghu Railway line. The Railway Bureau began a secret investigation, and occasionally discovered goods without waybills on trains between Wujin and Wuxi, which prompted close attention. Last month, Wang Xingen shipped ten pieces of smuggled yarn from Shanghai to Wuxi for delivery, but was discovered by the Railway Bureau, who sent police to follow him to Wuxi, preventing him from unloading the goods. He continued straight to Wujin. The Wujin station chief, seeing that he had no waybill, confronted him. Wang Xingen was handed over to the railway police and escorted to the Shanghai Railway Police Department for strict interrogation. Wang confessed to organizing a smuggling operation in Wuxi and implicated Station Chief Li Guisheng, Deputy Station Chief Shi Jintang, the heads of the freight and baggage departments, as well as more than ten other staff members, machinists, and workers. After learning of this, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Railway Bureau, was extremely angry. Believing that both the truth and the rumors should be thoroughly investigated, he sent Director Xiao to Wuxi to investigate. It is reported that Station Chief Li has been placed under surveillance. Other involved individuals have already left their positions under various pretexts, and Zhao Benli, Wang Xingen's partner, has fled to Dalian, effectively becoming a traitor.

Changshu: Farmer Beats Wife to Death 89

Qian Wuni, a farmer from Baiyuweng in the Eighth District, beat his wife, accidentally hitting her in the area of her lower back, causing her to suddenly laugh to death. Qian's wife, surnamed Gao, was 27 years old. One morning, before going to work in the field, Qian instructed Gao to sort out the wheat straw. However, when Qian returned home in the evening, the wheat straw was still untouched. Qian became angry and beat Gao with a bamboo pole. Accidentally, one foot kicked Gao in the lower back, a vital area, causing her to laugh to death on the spot. This year, the provincial government is implementing improved cotton production, starting with breeding. However, the drought has caused a huge loss.

Zhu Guochang, who runs the Dechang Bicycle Shop on Yangcheng Canfu Street, invited Liu Tonggeng, who runs a shoe shop inside Songfeng Alley, and a Mr. Yuan, who lives in Xiying, to ride bicycles to the outside of the South Gate for sightseeing this morning (the 1st). In the afternoon, Liu's father-in-law, Mr. Weng, led people out of the city to search. The body has not yet been recovered, and the bicycle is also missing.

Within the Second District, the banditry is rampant. On the evening of the 26th, two bandit boats with more than ten bandits armed with firearms arrived at Xiejiazhuang in Beining Township. After arriving at the village, they fired their guns as a warning and then separately looted various shops and residences. After three hours, they escaped with a full load of stolen goods. The Liu Taiyuan mill was robbed of 600 yuan in cash. Other shops, such as Zhu Jiuhong's silversmith shop, Zhang Faxin's grocery store, and Lu Yiyuan's sauce shop, suffered losses ranging from dozens to more than a hundred yuan. The losses to households were also mostly more than a hundred yuan. Unexpectedly, on the 28th, two more bandit boats came and robbed five or six families, seizing more than fifty stones of wheat. The village has suffered huge losses from the two robberies.

Hangzhou: 800,000 Autumn Silkworm Eggs Needed 94

The Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Association, considering that the summer silkworm season will end this month and preparations for the autumn silkworm season are urgently needed, reports that the total number of improved autumn silkworm eggs needed by various counties is 800,000 sheets. In addition to ordering and supplying half of them from the Zhejiang provincial breeding farms, the remaining 400,000 sheets will be purchased from the Jiangsu provincial breeding farms. To reduce the egg prices paid by farmers to 45 cents and to improve guidance work, 100 long-term instructors will be recruited. The exam will be held over three days, starting on July 1st, and the results should be announced next week.

Raising Funds to Repay Highway Construction Fees 95

More than 3,000 kilometers of highways in Zhejiang Province have been completed and opened to traffic. Transportation between eastern and western Zhejiang and the provincial capital has become increasingly convenient. However, due to the large construction costs, the provincial treasury is extremely stretched, resulting in arrears of approximately 3 million yuan in construction fees owed to contractors. After repeated petitions from the contractors for allocation of funds, the Construction Bureau issued more than 1 million yuan in local public bonds, so more than 2 million yuan has been repaid. The remaining 800,000 yuan will be issued and cleared at the end of this month by discounting the newly issued reorganization bonds. In addition, 3 million yuan in road funds borrowed from the Four Provinces Farmers Bank and the Dalu, Yanye, Zhongnan, and Jincheng Banks by the Construction Bureau last year. Except for more than 400,000 yuan that has been repaid successively, the remaining 1.6 million will be repaid by the Finance Department with public bonds.

Xiaoshan: Epidemic Raging in the City and Suburbs 96

In the past few days, the weather in Xiaoshan has been hot, and deaths from heatstroke among laborers have been frequent. In the city and suburbs, an epidemic is raging. Its initial symptoms are headache and fever. Within an hour, the hands and feet contract, and the patient becomes unconscious and unable to speak. Death occurs within a week. It is spreading uncontrollably in the city and outside the southeast gate. Since the 29th of last month, no fewer than dozens of people have died from the epidemic, and children are especially numerous among the victims. In order to prevent the epidemic, the county government has ordered the county hospital and Xiaoshan Hospital to administer vaccinations as a means of saving lives.

The Zhapu District Office, noting that the learning grain donation is heavily in arrears, sent police officers to the villages to collect it. Yesterday, the district chief sent the bao chief and another smoker surnamed Shen, along with the smoking paraphernalia, to the county for legal punishment.

Artistic Musings

The Art of the Fan (Part 1) 98

— Feng Zikai

Even in times of war and chaos, one can spare a little time to discuss the art of the fan waved by noble sons and grandsons.

The fan is a form of calligraphy and painting that has particularly flourished in China. This can also be regarded as one of the symbols of the Orient. In Western paintings that take Oriental themes, a folding fan is often used as an embellishment; and the humorous Spanish painters are very fond of using fans in their paintings. It is indeed a very leisurely thing. One does not need to work with one's hands, but simply waves the fan for one's own comfort; or even does not need to wave the fan, but simply looks at the calligraphy and painting on the fan for one's own visual pleasure. Is this not the clear bliss of a refined person? Therefore, it is reasonable for Westerners to like to use fans as a symbol of ancient Oriental customs. However, the art of painting fans is still a specialty of the Orientals. We have never seen fans depicted with pencil drawings, watercolor drawings, or oil paintings in Western paintings; conversely, in Chinese paintings, fan faces occupy a special position. In the fee schedules of calligraphers and painters, there is usually a "fan face" category, and some of them are particularly expensive; on the walls of mounting shops, there are often scrolls made of fan faces, which are regarded as a particularly elegant decoration in the study of scholars. This proves that in the past, painting art was particularly developed in China, not only were paintings hung everywhere in halls and rooms, but even the fan, a practical item for summer, was used by painters as a place to showcase their talents; thus, this practical item was "artified" and made into an art that was separated from practicality and independent, a "fan face for the sake of a fan face." It also proves that in the past, people's lives in China were particularly leisurely, not only did they have the time to wave a fan, but they had to wave a fan with paintings on it to seek comfort for both body and spirit, a comfortable unity of body and soul.

Therefore, both the painting methods of fans and the uses of fans are artistic specialties of the Chinese people. When it comes to painting methods, because its outline shape is special, the layout of the painting also has a different approach. Most painting materials are suitable for using parts of objects—such as a broken branch of flowers, a part of a bamboo forest, or fruit hanging in the air. Or, it is suitable to use scenery that does not show the horizon—such as continuous mountains, undulating jungles, or scenery covered by clouds and fog. In short, it is not suitable to show the horizon on the fan face, because the outline is arc-shaped, and the horizon line runs from the upper left corner to the upper right corner, dividing the fan into jagged upper and lower parts, which is unaesthetic. In Chinese fan paintings, figure paintings are relatively few, because figures must have houses as a background, and houses are square things, which easily show the horizon, which hinders the composition. Landscape paintings are the most numerous, because landscapes are high and low, left and right, and the horizon line can be concealed everywhere, making it easy to arrange the painting. Fortunately, there is no fan face category in Western painting; if there were, Western painters would be worried to death about the composition! Because Western paintings pay the same attention to the background as to the main object. There is no painting without a background. In Chinese paintings, there is often a painting method in which there is no background at all, and the main object is suspended in a blank sheet of paper. But from the perspective of Western painting, these are unfinished works. If Westerners were taught to paint, they would have to add many things behind, either the sky or the ground, and must express the place where the main object is located. Therefore, Western paintings must have a background, must conform to the laws of perspective, that is, must have a horizon line. In the outline of the fan face, it is difficult to arrange it properly. Perhaps this is also one of the reasons why fan paintings have flourished in China. The imaginative, irrelevant, and patterned Chinese paintings can be cleverly packed into any outline. This can also be said to be a feature of Oriental art.

Book Industry Dispute Comes to an End: Price Increases Temporarily Suspended 101

New Regulations Postponed for Six Months: Wholesale Prices Follow Ministry Guidelines

According to Huadong News Agency, the Shanghai Book Industry Association had previously noted that the price suppression by vendors was detrimental to the book market. Therefore, in accordance with the sales regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Education in April, the association formulated new wholesale standards and discount prices in fifteen chapters and sixty-four articles, which were originally scheduled to take effect on July 1st (the day before yesterday). However, due to the opposition of the vendors to these regulations, the executive committee resolved to temporarily suspend the price increases. The new regulations will be postponed for six months (i.e., January 1, 1937). At present, wholesale prices will only follow the ten price guidelines issued by the Ministry. It is reported that the vendors have been discussing the next steps.

Claims Fujian-Guangdong Border is Currently Peaceful

To Proceed to Nanjing Tomorrow Evening to Attend the Second Plenary Session

He is staying at the residence of his relative, Mr. Zhang, on Muirhead Road. He is scheduled to proceed to Nanjing by train tomorrow evening. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency paid him a special visit. According to Mr. Chen:

No Trouble on the Fujian Border: In the Longyan area of southwestern Fujian Province, a small number of unruly elements from the old disbanded local militias are constantly looking for opportunities to disrupt the peace. Therefore, Director Jiang (Dingwen) dispatched troops to suppress them. The sole purpose is to maintain local order. It appears that Guangdong Province is mobilizing its troops, but they have not yet crossed into Fujian. The border between the two provinces remains peaceful. As for other areas within the province, everything is very calm and there are no signs of unrest.

A Turning Point in the Current Situation: It is said that the southwest region will definitely send representatives to attend the Second Plenary Session, but the candidates are unknown. The turning point in the current situation will depend on the Second Plenary Session. It is regrettable that some comrades in the southwest cannot understand the Central Government's difficult position in dealing with the national crisis. It is essential to understand that to speak of resisting foreign aggression, the whole country must be united. There should be no local actions, and personal prejudices should not be stubbornly adhered to, causing chaos. Otherwise, local losses will be minor, but the country's losses will be significant. Looking at the current situation, the local losses in Guangdong and Guangxi are already evident, such as the sharp drop in currency value. The people of the two provinces are already full of complaints. Hopefully, Mr. Chen, Mr. Li, and Mr. Bai will come to their senses after being advised by all parties.

Party Affairs and Officialdom: Mr. Chen continued, stating that Fujian's party affairs have seen progress in recent years. In the past two years, the focus has been on self-organization. Now, efforts are being intensified to train the people and organize mass groups, which have become more robust. As for formal elections and the restoration of the provincial party headquarters, the Central Government has not yet set a date. This is because some provinces have established party headquarters with a committee system, while others have a simple system with special envoys appointed by the Central Government. The Central Government is currently comparing and studying the advantages and disadvantages of the simple system versus the committee system. Since the implementation of the supervisory commissioner system in Fujian, judicial and political personnel have been more honest than before. Currently, most of the cases received by the supervisory commissioner's office involve lower-ranking officials such as district chiefs and joint guarantee directors. Some county magistrates have also been accused, mostly in connection with surcharges on land taxes. In terms of provincial administration, since Chairman Chen (Yi) took office, there has been significant progress. Although some plans have not been realized immediately, the overall situation is good. For example, in terms of road construction, last year it was only in a rough state, but now the roadbeds have been consolidated. Mr. Chen concluded by saying that he is scheduled to proceed to Nanjing by train on the evening of the fourth to attend the meeting of regional supervisory commissioners on the fifth and to prepare for the Second Plenary Session.
