Post and Telegraph Offices at Stations Along Both Railways Also Sell Stamp Tax Tickets 113

Implemented Since the First of This Month

For the convenience of merchants and travelers, the Postal Administration has sent a letter to the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus requesting that stamp tax tickets also be sold at the post and telegraph offices at the nine major stations along the lines. Each station will first be pre-issued ten yuan of stamp tax tickets by the local post office. Afterwards, in accordance with the method of selling stamps on consignment, they will submit a list at any time to the local post office to request for more. The post office will issue remuneration on a quarterly basis, calculated at one percent based on the actual number of stamps sold by each agency per quarter, with a maximum of ten yuan and a minimum of ten cents. The Bureau believes that this measure is indeed beneficial to merchants and travelers and has replied to comply with the instructions. It has been implemented since the first of the month.

The Party and National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau Hosted a Press Reception Yesterday Regarding Flag Prices 114

Detailed Account of the Deliberation and Determination of Flag Prices, Demonstrating the Proportion of the Current Price Reduction

The Party and National Flag Manufacturing and Sales Bureau initially suffered from rumors, leading outsiders to suspect that the raw materials for its flag manufacturing were not entirely domestic products. Some even disregarded the facts and publicly criticized it in writing. The Bureau then openly invited people from all walks of life to visit on May 7th to prove the fact that it spins, weaves, prints, and dyes its own materials. This was to ensure that people from all walks of life would know that all raw materials, except for the dyes, were entirely domestic products, so that fair-minded people would not be deceived. Afterwards, those who intentionally criticized the Bureau, unable to find fault with the raw materials and technology, turned to criticizing the flag prices. The 46th Branch of the Citizens' Joint Association of the First Special District of Shanghai successively sent letters to the General Association requesting it to submit a petition to the Party and government authorities to reduce prices. In addition to replying factually, the Bureau specifically hosted a banquet for the press yesterday to report on the facts of the pricing process. Many representatives from various newspapers attended. First, Zhang Zilian, the chairman of the Bureau's Committee, delivered a speech, stating that before the central government promulgated the standards for Party and National Flag printing and dyeing, the flags sold on the market were all pieced together and sewn together from faded flags, and the raw materials for the cloth were mostly foreign goods. I believe that you all understand that after this Bureau adopted the process of independently spinning, weaving, printing, dyeing, and completing the entire process of making the Party and National Flag, it prepared a detailed cost budget by item in accordance with the flag manufacturing and sales procedures and submitted it to the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of the Interior for approval. In addition to sending personnel to conduct on-site inspections in accordance with the budget items, the two departments also purchased various flags sold on the market at that time, referred to the prices in the purchase invoices, and negotiated the first flag price. According to the market price of flags at that time, a No. 6 flag cost between 2.4 yuan and 2.8 yuan, which was already more than 13% lower than the market price of flags at that time. Afterwards, in order to care for the people's hardships, the two departments considered selling more and reducing the burden on the people as much as possible, and negotiated the second flag price. The second flag price of the No. 6 flag was set at 2 yuan per flag, which was 30% lower than the market price of flags sold previously. From the purely commercial point of view, the price set was actually too low. The flags sold on the market were made of multiple pieces of cloth, pieced together and sewn together, and the color would fade after being exposed to the sun and rain. The raw materials for the flag cloth were mostly foreign goods. The flags currently made are made independently in one piece, and the color will not fade after being exposed to the sun and rain. The raw materials for the flag cloth, starting from the cotton used for spinning, are all domestic products. Therefore, the technology of the material and spirit of the flag is far superior to that of the flags sold on the market before. Logically, the material spirit and technology of the flag are far superior to the flags sold previously, which were pieced together, sewn together, and easily faded. The raw materials, except for the pigments, are all purely domestic products. Rewards should be given for progress in improving the material, expressing the spirit, and improving the technology. The flag prices should be slightly increased compared to the original flag prices sold on the market as the cost of correcting the material, expressing the spirit, and improving the technology. Today, we have not only not demanded this cost, but also absolutely abandoned the concept of reasonable commercial profit, respected the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of the Interior's main purpose of considering the people's hardships, and unconditionally obeyed the repeatedly reduced flag prices. The purpose of our manufacturing and selling the Party and National Flags is entirely as stated in the promotional declaration: to awaken the heavy-laden hearts of the people who are lying in wait for the time to resist aggression, and to do our best to fulfill our national duty. We have not paid attention to profit-seeking. This can prove that even a very small number of people with selfish ideas still do not want to face the facts and forcefully criticize without purpose, causing fair-minded people to be deceived again. This is not because we oppose criticizing the flag prices, but because their criticism lacks reasonable facts and evidence. Those who want to criticize the flag prices as expensive must have a comparison of facts or be able to cite evidence that the flag prices sold on the market before were indeed cheaper than the currently set flag prices, or have concrete facts sufficient to prove that the cost of the flag, which is equally in line with the Central Printing and Dyeing Law's standards, is indeed lower than the flag manufacturing budget set by this Bureau. Today, the criticizers have failed to cite these facts or evidence, making it impossible for people to believe that they have no ulterior motive. Previously, in order to appease people, this Bureau did not want to pursue legal action against this matter. Now, due to the pressure of the situation, we may no longer be allowed to maintain the value of forgiveness. We have specifically reported the process of deliberating and setting the flag prices, and the fact that the currently set flag prices are indeed 30% lower than the flag prices sold on the market before, to everyone, and explained the flag manufacturing and sales budget. Please understand the facts, give a fair evaluation, and hope that those who intentionally criticize in vain can focus on the overall situation, be aware of the reality, and no longer create tortuous and cunning ways to deceive fair-minded people. Others have said that our responsibility to have the entire nation hang national flags is a manifestation of the people's spirit of loving the country and the nation. This manifestation of spirit is sufficient to make the government believe that it has a reliable support, and to make all countries value the unified public opinion. Its significance is equivalent to the popular vote in Germany to support the leader's policies. If those who intentionally criticize in vain persist in their views of love and hatred, which cannot be changed, and are determined to destroy this Bureau's task of undertaking the manufacture of Party and National Flags, then this Bureau is also happy to transfer the right to undertake the task. As for the form of national economic decline, we should present to the Central Government that those who are unable to purchase No. 6 flags in their households should be allowed to purchase No. 5 flags. The previous market price of No. 5 flags was about 1.5 yuan per flag. Recently, this Bureau received an invoice from the Ningbo branch for the purchase of this flag, which was 1.3 yuan. The flag's style is still made of multiple pieces of cloth, pieced together and sewn together, while the current flag price set by this Bureau is 90 cents, which is 66% lower than the previous market price and 33% lower than the purchased flag invoice price. With the above facts, the difficulty of further price reductions is evident. In order to respect public sentiment and care for the people's hardships, the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of the Interior have twice specifically invited representatives from this Bureau to talk. As a result of the talks, the flag manufacturing and sales budget presented to the Central Government was studied, and in order to comply with the situation, it was proposed to reduce distribution costs in order to reduce flag prices. However, it was also feared that once distribution costs were reduced, the sales ability might be reduced. New marketing methods are currently being planned to achieve the best of both worlds. The colleagues of this Bureau, who are responsible for manufacturing and selling the Party and National Flags, have conducted in-depth research on the significance of promoting the Party and National Flags. In addition to revealing part of the significance in the published promotional declaration, we have specifically excerpted three suggestions from the original submission to Chairman Chiang, and respectfully ask all of you who have graced us with your presence today for your guidance. After finishing the speech, the banquet concluded and dispersed.

Match United Company to be Established Next Week; Chinese and Japanese Manufacturers to Inspect North China 122

According to the Ta Kung Pao, a joint production and sales general office will be formed by Chinese match manufacturers and Japanese match factories in various parts of China. This was vigorously promoted by leading figures in the Chinese and Japanese match industries, Liu Hongsheng, Longchuan, and Ueda, and realized after being supported by all Chinese and Japanese match manufacturers. The joint venture's capital is set at 5 million yuan, with the Chinese side contributing 75%, accounting for 3.75 million yuan of the total, and the Japanese side contributing 25%, accounting for 1.25 million yuan of the total. Currently, this capital is allocated among Chinese and Japanese factories according to their original capital ratio, with many factories subscribing to shares. The Da Zhonghua Match Factory in this city holds 20% of the total shares, so the joint venture's capital has already been fully subscribed.

Inspect North China A national match united company jointly formed by Chinese and Japanese businesses has been actively progressing on various tasks since its organizational preparation. To understand the current situation of manufacturers in Pingjin and Qingdao, the Chinese side has specifically dispatched representatives Xu Zhiyi and Liu Qinghe, and the Japanese side representative Ueda, who jointly went to North China for inspection in mid-last month. They are also planning to establish branch offices in Tianjin (North China region) and Qingdao (Lu-Yu region). According to the Ta Kung Pao reporter's investigation, the group of Chinese and Japanese manufacturers' representatives has completed their inspection and will return to Shanghai tomorrow to report.

To be Established Next Week The capital for the Sino-Japanese joint match production and sales company has long been raised, and all articles of association and business regulations have also been drafted. They will be submitted to the Ministry of Industry for record after being approved by the founding meeting. As for the board seats, the Chinese side will get six-tenths, and the Japanese side will get four-tenths. The general manager will also be appointed by the Chinese side, and two deputy general managers will be appointed, one from the Chinese side and one from the Japanese side. Internally, there will be departments for general affairs, statistics, investigation, production, sales, and auditing.

Adopting Control A Ta Kung Pao reporter also learned from reliable sources that after the establishment of the joint head office, all Chinese and Japanese match manufacturers' rights to production and sales will be managed by the company in a controlled manner. Prices will be unified by grade, and both parties will be restricted from adding new factories. Only member manufacturers of the joint company will be able to enjoy business rights, and their sales will be restricted. The business volume between China and Japan will be determined according to the capital, with Chinese merchants accounting for about seven-tenths and Japanese merchants accounting for about three-tenths.

American Business Exits There were rumors that the American-owned Swedish American Micron Match Factory would also join the joint venture and combine its business. However, the Ta Kung Pao reporter learned that due to unresolved negotiation conditions, the Japanese side also expressed little support for the American business joining. Therefore, this proposal was implicitly dismissed. The American business also voluntarily withdrew because the terms of the joint production and sales were too harsh. However, the investigation showed that the scope of the American match factory's market share in China is gradually shrinking, which has no major impact on the prospects of the joint venture.

Rescuing Vessels in Distress 125

Towing Stranded Vessels The Fengpu Wheel of the Sanbei Company has been stranded in the middle of the Three Mountains in Nanjing for six days. The Songpu Wheel was initially sent to tow it, but it was unsuccessful and also became stranded. The company received a telegram from the owner of the Fengpu Wheel yesterday, stating that the Jiangyu Wheel of the China Merchants Bureau was used to tow it, but the first attempt was still unsuccessful. However, the water gauge has now been measured, showing sixteen feet on the outside and only ten feet on the inside. It has been decided to wait for the high tide this morning (3rd) and hope to rescue it. The Songpu Wheel was fully loaded with coal from Tongzibao to Zhenjiang (not transporting salt). The Changxing Wheel was used to tow it, but because the Songpu Wheel was drawing too much water, it was stranded even more severely and could not be moved. The shipowner telegraphed back and forth with the Shanghai company, and as a result, it was decided to send a large barge to the Three Mountains to unload 500 tons of coal to Nanjing, and then lighten the Songpu Wheel's draft and send a ship to rescue it and tow it out of the shallows.

Tongli Wheel Rushed by Waves The Tongli Wheel of the Tianjin Shipping Company, with a deadweight of 2,260 tons, was heading to Haizhou to load salt. The ship was anchored at Lvzikou when it suddenly encountered a storm and huge waves. The Tongli Wheel was washed onto the beach by the wind and waves and became stranded. Finally, due to the force of the huge waves, it broke free from the beach. However, the ship's wire rope was broken, and the horizontal bar of the anchor was also broken. According to the shipowner's report yesterday, whether the hull was damaged is still unclear and will be known after inspection.

Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau Reissues New Water, Electricity, and Transportation Licenses 128

The Shanghai Public Utilities Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that the validity period of the following water, electricity, and transportation licenses issued by the Bureau in the 25th year of the Republic of China all expired at the end of June of this year. According to the usual practice, new licenses for the 26th year should be reissued starting from July 1st. This year, in accordance with the order to unify the license renewal method, after this license renewal, except for licenses for small cars, cargo ships, and rowing boats, which still need to be renewed annually, the remaining licenses only need to be sent to the Bureau for review once a year during the prescribed period in July of each year to save procedures. Currently, the new licenses for water and electricity merchants, as well as small cars, cargo ships, and rowing boats, have all been prepared and will be reissued as scheduled. The new licenses for electrical material stores, electrical contractors, and automobile gas stations are still being printed. Once they are completed, another notice will be issued to schedule the renewal. All licensed households in the city should be aware of this. This is hereby announced. July 1st to 15th: reissue licenses for water and electricity merchants, electrical material stores, electrical contractors, and automobile gas stations. July 1st to 21st: reissue licenses for small cars, cargo ships, and rowing boats.

Pioneer in the Transportation Industry; Huang Zhongwen Returns from the United States After Studying; He Will Make Novel Contributions to the Domestic Transportation Industry 133

The Huashang Public Bus Company, the only transportation hub in Zhabei, has been established for many years and has made great contributions to the society and the people. Mr. Huang Zhongwen, the general manager of the company, lived overseas in his early years and helped the late Premier Sun Yat-sen in his revolutionary work. When the foundation of the Republic of China was established, he retired to become a businessman. After Huang founded the Huashang Company, all the plans were implemented step by step. Although the scale was slightly inferior to that of the British company, the internal organization was more rigorous and thorough than any other company. The business has been booming in the past three years, and Huang's ambition to make progress has never been slackened. Last year, he made a special trip to the United States to study the various evolutions of the transportation industry, which lasted for more than half a year. He completed his great mission the day before yesterday and returned with a wealth of novel knowledge about the transportation industry, which he will gradually realize and make great contributions to the society and the country. According to Mr. Huang, he has successively inspected more than 30 transportation hubs in various cities. There are as many as ten kinds of the latest invented cars that save fuel or increase speed. Among them, the most valuable is the three-tire car (recently invented by the Seattle Cebopin Company), which saves 50% more gasoline than the same car, and the price is surprisingly cheap, only half the price of the same-sized car. It can also be said to be an amazing discovery in the transportation industry. He has signed an operating rights contract with the company. If the environment permits, he will set up manufacturing or sales agencies to help the domestic transportation construction. Other examples include sleeper double-decker cars, and cars that use "gasoline vapor" as fuel, which can also save 50%, but are not easy to store.

Nanjing Road; The Citizens' Association Sends a Letter to the Public Works Bureau Requesting a Refund of Overpaid House Tax for Member Stores 134

The Nanjing Road Citizens' First District Branch sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau yesterday on behalf of its member stores, Taikang Company, Zhonghua Photo Studio, Hongxiang Company, and Shanghai Old Goods Store, requesting a refund of overpaid tax. The original letter is excerpted as follows: We would like to inform you that we have recently received a joint letter from our member stores, Taikang Company, Zhonghua Photo Studio, Hongxiang Company, and Shanghai Old Goods Store on Nanjing Road, stating that our company has been renting houses on Nanjing Road. Last year, we requested the landlords to reduce the rent, which was approved by the landlords and implemented from April of last year. The Public Works Bureau's collection of house tax has always been based on the amount of rent. Since the rent has been reduced, the house tax should of course be reduced proportionally. However, at that time, in order to negotiate a rent reduction with the landlords, we were afraid that it would take time and hinder the tax collection, so when the Public Works Bureau collected the house tax, we still paid according to the amount before the reduction. However, we stated that if there was any overpayment after the rent reduction issue was resolved, we would request a refund or deduction. Later, the rent reduction issue was resolved. We have repeatedly requested the Tax Collection Office to refund the overpaid tax, but they only agreed to reduce the tax collection from January of this year. They refused to accept the amount that should have been reduced for the summer, autumn, and winter seasons of last year, totaling nine months. Now, our companies, except for Taikang Company, which has already paid the house tax for this year, are still waiting for the refund of the overpaid amount for the summer, autumn, and winter seasons of the 24th year of the Republic of China. Hongxiang and others have requested that the past overpaid amount be used to offset the tax to save procedures. However, we recently received a serious warning from the Public Works Bureau, requiring us to clear the unpaid tax in full before July 4th, otherwise they will file a public lawsuit. It is justifiable for our companies to request that the overpaid amount be used to offset the tax, and it is not comparable to resisting tax payment. There is no reason to file a public lawsuit. We hereby urge your association to uphold justice and appeal to the Public Works Bureau to uphold justice and maintain the hardship of merchants. We found that in the 24th year of the Republic of China last year, the Jicheng Pharmacy at No. 166 Nanjing Road also temporarily paid the tax because the rent reduction issue had not been resolved. Later, the rent was reduced, and on September 26 of the same year, it received a notice from the Tax Collection Office of your bureau to refund the overpaid tax. The case of Taikang Company and others is the same, and should be considered. We hope that you will investigate and deal with it in accordance with the previous case, and please reply.

New Prison Completed in Beixinjing, Pusong District; Prisoners in Special Prison No. 2 Have Been Transferred to the New Prison; Special Prison No. 1 and Jiangsu Second Branch Prison Will Also Be Moved 138

The Ministry of Judicial Administration, considering that the First and Second Special District Prisons in this city are small and insufficient to accommodate prisoners, and that the Jiangsu Second Branch Prison on North Zhejiang Road and the Special Second Detention Center on Xuehuali Road are poorly equipped, spent money two years ago to purchase hundreds of acres of land in Beixinjing, Pusong District, Shanghai West, to build a huge prison, intending to move the convicted prisoners of the First and Second Special District Courts to the new prison, and convert the original two prisons into detention centers. Because the new prison has been under construction for a long time, it has now been completed one after another. On the 28th of last month, it instructed the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court to order the Special Second Prison and Detention Center to move the prisoners in custody to the new prison starting from the 1st of this month, and move the unconvicted persons in the detention center to the original Special Second Prison. Sun Xiong, the warden of the Special Second Prison, will temporarily concurrently serve as the head of the detention center, and Jiang Fengyi, the former head of the Special Second Detention Center, will be reassigned as a prison official. Sun and Jiang were ordered to start transferring and detaining all convicted and unconvicted persons separately from 3:00 PM on the 1st. The name of the new prison is the Second Prison directly under the Ministry of Judicial Administration. It is heard that the Special First Prison and the Jiangsu Second Branch Prison will also begin to move, but the staff of the Special Second Detention Center, including 60 detention center personnel, have not received orders from the Ministry and do not know whether they will be dismissed. The Special Second Warden, who is also the head of the detention center, has telegraphed the Ministry of Judicial Administration for instructions. Before receiving orders from the Ministry, they will continue to provide food and lodging every day.

Abandoning the Old and Embracing the New: A Cycle of Retribution – Zheng Shiyue Accuses Chen Mingxun – Demanding a Hefty Sum of 144,000 Yuan for Living Expenses – Summons for the Defendant Unsuccessful, Hearing Adjourned to a Later Date 139

Zheng Shiyue, a woman from Ningbo, currently 20 years old and possessing some beauty, was married to Gu Chengda, a fellow villager, through a matchmaker on the 4th day of the fourth month of the lunar calendar in the 21st year of the Republic [1932]. Later, Zheng worked as a saleswoman for the British American Tobacco Company, earning a monthly salary of approximately 70-80 yuan. Due to her work, around September of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], she met Chen Mingxun (age 30), a native of Haiyan and owner of the Rixin Chang Foreign Goods Store at No. 29, Lane 240, Avenue Edward VII. At that time, Chen used all sorts of enticements and exploited his power to force himself upon her, and they had relations at the Nanjing Hotel. Because Zheng already had a husband, Chen Mingxun instigated her to separate from her husband, claiming that he himself was unmarried and that if she divorced, he would marry her. Zheng believed him, and she negotiated a divorce with Gu Chengda. As a result, on December 26th of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], they signed a divorce agreement, with lawyer Huang Xiuqi as the witness. The condition was that Zheng would pay Gu 360 yuan to settle the matter. After Zheng Shiyue achieved her goal of divorce, she cohabited with Chen at No. 1, Derun Lane, Rue Luson, and No. 1370, Avenue Edward VII, and Chen gave Zheng 300 yuan per month for living expenses. However, after cohabiting for many months, Chen never indicated any intention to marry Zheng Shiyue. Despite her urging, Chen always procrastinated. This spring, Chen suddenly changed, finding another love and becoming disgusted with Zheng. He even stopped paying for living expenses. Zheng Shiyue then hired lawyer Wang Liangqing and filed a lawsuit against Chen in the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court, accusing him of seduction and abandonment, requesting that he be punished according to the first half of Article 240, Section 2, and Article 239 of the Criminal Law, and additionally requesting Chen Mingxun to pay 300 yuan per month for living expenses until she reached the age of 60, totaling 144,000 yuan in national currency. Yesterday afternoon, judge Huang Daxi of the First Special Court opened the Fifth Criminal Court for a hearing. Because the summons for Chen Mingxun could not be delivered, only Zheng Shiyue was questioned, and the hearing was adjourned to a later date.

A Comic Scene – A Blind Man Catches an Adulterer – Father-in-Law Supports Son-in-Law in Lawsuit – Blind in Eye, Not Blind in Heart 140

Ni Heting, a native of Ningbo, is blind in one eye and works as a fortune teller. He has a daughter named Yunmei, who is only sixteen years old and also blind in one eye. His son-in-law, Fu Atang, is also blind. Moreover, the father-in-law and son-in-law share the same profession. However, only half a month after Fu married Yunmei on May 30th of this year, a comic scene of "a blind man catching an adulterer" occurred. Now, according to Ni Heting, the girl's father, he has filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, stating that Qiu Hongkui, a fellow villager residing at No. 307, Yuezhou Road, suddenly broke into his son-in-law's house at 9:00 PM on the 17th of last month and raped his daughter Yunmei. He has cited his daughter and son-in-law as witnesses, requesting an investigation. Yesterday afternoon, judge Zhong Qing opened a court session and summoned the plaintiff, defendant, and witnesses Fu Atang and Ni Yunmei, a total of four people. Only Qiu's eyes were unharmed. The Ni father and daughter still had one eye that could see. The summons was brought to the court with the support of his father-in-law. According to the testimony, when Qiu was raping his wife, he happened to return from outside and heard his wife panting. He entered the room to question her, but Qiu, thinking he was blind, tried to escape. Although he was blind in eye, he was not blind in heart. He listened to the footsteps and guessed that the person was Qiu. He immediately grabbed him and so on. However, Qiu claimed that the plaintiff and others were making false accusations because they had failed to borrow money. Judge Zhong declared that the case was related to public morals and required a detailed investigation, so he announced that the hearing was closed to the public.

Regulations for the Management of Beverages by the French Concession Municipal Council – A Total of Six Articles 144

The Regulations for the Management of Beverage Sales by the French Concession Municipal Council have been established and are promulgated as follows: Article 1: The display, sale, or serving of counterfeit or harmful beverages is strictly prohibited. Article 2: All labels or signs clearly displayed on bottles, pots, or other containers of beverages prepared for sale or serving must detail the nature, ingredients, or place of origin of the ingredients, and the manufacturing method of the beverage. Article 3: If beverages prepared for sale or serving are contained in containers without clear labels or signs, the nature, ingredients, or place of origin of the ingredients, and the manufacturing method of the beverage must be clearly stated in the price list, product list, posters, or menus presented to buyers or consumers. Article 4: The contents of beverages contained in various containers as stipulated in the aforementioned Articles 2 and 3 must match the descriptions stated on the labels or signs, and in the price lists, product lists, posters, or menus. Article 5: Anyone who violates these regulations shall be subject to a fine of between 50 yuan and 1,000 yuan, and the beverages displayed, sold, or served in violation of the regulations shall be confiscated. If such violations constitute a serious or minor crime, the offender shall still be prosecuted according to the law. If a classified business commits a violation of these regulations, it shall be punished in accordance with the provisions of the last two sections of Article 15 of the Municipal Council's Regulations for the Management of Classified Businesses. Article 6: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Municipal Government Notice: Licensed Opium Smokers – Limited to One Set of Smoking Paraphernalia 145

The Municipal Government posted Notice No. 4292 on the 1st of this month, stating: "It has been reported that the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Opium Prohibition Crimes have been revised by the Chairman of the National Government Military Commission and Concurrent Commissioner-General for Opium Prohibition on June 18th and submitted to the National Government, which officially promulgated them on June 3rd and issued them for implementation. Hereafter, those who have obtained a limited-term opium abstinence license shall be limited to one set of equipment specifically for smoking opium; the rest shall be ordered to be destroyed. If the individual dies or has quit the opium habit, the family or the individual shall return the smoking paraphernalia along with the license; violators shall be treated as possessing smoking paraphernalia in accordance with the regulations. Let this be widely known. In addition to ordering the Public Security Bureau to comply, this notice is hereby given to be widely known." After receiving the instructions from the Municipal Government, the Public Security Bureau has issued strict orders to all sub-bureaus to conduct thorough investigations and warn licensed opium smokers to quickly hand over their surplus smoking paraphernalia to the bureau for destruction. If multiple sets of smoking paraphernalia are secretly kept, even if there is no establishment of opium dens for people to smoke, it will be treated as secret possession of smoking paraphernalia, which is also a violation of the law. In accordance with the provisions of Article 16 of the recently revised and promulgated Provisional Regulations for Punishing Opium Prohibition Crimes by the National Government, the offender shall be sentenced to imprisonment for up to one year or a fine of up to 500 yuan.

Shanghai's Southern Goods Industry (Continued) Compiled by China Credit Bureau

(Thirty of the Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce)

8. Business Overview

The Southern Goods industry is involved in the sale of food items. Because of its wide variety, it can also be called a food department store. Therefore, its business scope is quite broad. In the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic of China, there were nearly three million residents in Shanghai who came from other provinces. Agriculture was thriving, prices were low, the social economy was abundant, and the money lending industry was relaxed. Anyone who operated this business and had a certain reputation could obtain loans even if they lacked capital. In addition to providing working capital, money lending businesses also provided long-term loans. Therefore, the economy was very smooth, and the business of extending credit also expanded accordingly. The Southern Goods and Exchange industry extended credit, and accounting was settled during the Dragon Boat Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, and Lunar New Year, known as the three festivals. After settlement, credit was extended again, and the loans had to be repaid in February or March of the following year. As a result, the business developed greatly. Small Southern Goods stores in towns within 200 li of the city all did business with the Southern Goods Exchange industry in this city. The annual business volume reached 2.7 million yuan, and there were many profits. Therefore, more than 200 companies in the same industry sprang up, which was the golden age of the industry.

In the last ten years, because various parts of the country have been plagued by natural disasters and foreign invasions, the rural economy has gone bankrupt. Furthermore, the Northeast was lost, and the Shanghai war caused severe damage. Domestic industry and commerce are exhausted, the economic panic is increasingly profound, purchasing power is weak, and business has sharply declined. The money lending industry has also become increasingly tight, so those who were unable to maintain their businesses, including the well-known Nan San Mao, Bei San Mao, Xin Tai Sheng, Lao Tai Sheng, and Hong Tai, all successively closed down. Many other companies with weak financial strength have also collapsed. According to people in the industry, the business volume of this industry in recent years is only 40% to 50% of its peak period.

Business Investigation

The Southern Goods industry has a wide scope, and the number of businesses in the same industry has increased daily. There are also distinctions between different provincial guilds. Therefore, its business is scattered. Later, in order to seek the development of business and resolve disputes, the Zhejiang guild first proposed the establishment of Chun Ze Tang in the Guangxu years as a trade association. However, it still maintained private opinions and sought to maintain balance. The Ningbo guild then established Yong Xing Hui, and the local Shanghai guild also established Chong Yi Tang to handle their respective affairs. Chun Ze Tang is located in Tangfang Lane outside Xiaonantou and was established the earliest. In the third year of the Republic of China, it was renamed the Southern and Northern Goods Exchange Industry Trade Association. It has considerable real estate and abundant funds. Only 17 members are from both the southern and northern markets, and all other businesses in the same industry and new businesses are not allowed to join. It has a monopoly nature. Chong Yi Tang is located on Ninghe Road in the western part of the city and has been established for more than 30 years. In the fourth year of the Republic of China, it was renamed the Southern Goods Industry Trade Association. Yong Xing Hui merged into Chong Yi Tang in the 22nd year of the Republic of China, with more than 100 members. However, funds are depleted and income does not cover expenses.

According to investigations, there are only more than 220 businesses in the same industry in this city today. Among them, more than 100 are called major businesses (i.e., members of the association) and have the right to directly purchase goods from the market. Half of those who have not joined the association are sold by Shi He Da Tong Hang (i.e., members of the association) in wholesale or sold to the Southern and Northern Goods Exchange industry. The business names of each company are listed below:

Chun Ze Tang Public Office—i.e., Southern and Northern Goods Exchange Trade Association, with 17 members in total:

Letter

Dear Editor,

According to Li Cao, the party concerned, after reading the news item titled "Daughter-in-Law Accuses Father-in-Law" on page 15 of the fourth section of the Shen Bao on July 2, the content is all one-sided and contains many inaccuracies. The small-print headline "Addicted to Gambling and Violating Family Rules" is deliberately defamatory, which is deeply regrettable. It is found that because Ms. Li Cao could not bear the abuse of her mother-in-law, her father, Lan Bin, and her father-in-law, Li Hong, agreed that her father-in-law would provide her with a monthly living allowance of 80 yuan to allow her to live separately. Over the years, they have been getting along well. Unexpectedly, starting in March of this year, her father-in-law suddenly stopped the monthly allowance. After unsuccessful attempts to persuade him, she had no choice but to take her children to beg him. However, he treated them as strangers and drove them out. Having reached the end of the road and having no way to compromise, she had no choice but to seek legal relief. The report in the newspaper is clearly not the truth. Please send a letter to the newspaper to correct the facts and clarify the truth.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Bao Zhihui

Kang Ti Tennis Club Organizes Member Ranking Tournament

Thirty members divided into groups A and B. In order to promote the tennis skills of its members, the Kang Ti Tennis Club is organizing a member ranking tournament. The method is to divide all members into several levels and hold competitions. The ranking will be determined based on the results of the competition to increase the members' interest in competition and improve their tennis skills invisibly. The rules and member ranking list are listed below:

The initial ranking of the member ranking tournament is determined by the Competition Committee based on the members' tennis skills.

Any lower-ranked member may request to compete with a member ranked ahead of them or with a member in the row ahead of them. After winning, they may advance to a higher ranking.

The challenged party must accept this challenge within two weeks, otherwise, it will be considered a waiver, and the ranking will be switched with the challenger.

Winners do not have to accept challenges from lower-ranked members and have the right to challenge higher-ranked members. However, this does not apply if they do not challenge a higher-ranked member within two weeks of winning.

Losers cannot challenge higher-ranked members and must accept challenges from lower-ranked members. However, this does not apply if they do not accept any challenges within two weeks.

The challenger must notify the club staff at least 72 hours before the match so that a venue can be designated.

All ranking matches will be played in a best-of-three-sets format.

The club will provide new balls for each match. The cost is 2 yuan for three Spolding balls and 1.5 yuan for three Dunjop balls. The cost of the balls will be paid by the loser. The old balls will be collected by the club after the match.

If a player is more than ten minutes late for a match, it will be considered a waiver.

The Competition Committee has the right to add or modify the regulations as needed.

National Arts Athletes, Life on the Ship

Hong Kong Correspondence: The National Arts Delegation to the World Games boarded the Conte Verde in Shanghai on the 26th and left the country. That night, manager Hao Mingjun gathered all the team members and stipulated that during the voyage, they would train in group Taijiquan exercises on the deck from 5:00 AM to 6:00 AM every morning and practice various paired boxing and weapons routines. This began the next day (27th). However, the national arts team members were traveling abroad for the first time and were not accustomed to the sea voyage and the ship's swaying. Therefore, they felt somewhat uncomfortable with life. The exercises made them feel even more dizzy. By the second training session on the morning of the 28th, the team members had gradually become accustomed to the sea voyage and became more interested and energetic. At 2:00 PM, the ship arrived in Hong Kong and responded to the grand send-off party held by the Hong Kong China Northern Athletic Association. Swimming representatives Chen Zhenxing and Yang Xiuqiong boarded the ship that evening. They were very interested in the national arts team's weapons routines. There is something worth reporting to the national arts comrades in Shanghai, namely, that the sports community has always been somewhat indifferent to the national arts and has different views. This time, everyone gathered on the same ship and spent time together day and night. Everyone gradually recognized the subtleties of the national arts and gained the sympathy of the majority. The national arts team members also deeply felt the importance of this trip. Therefore, they immersed themselves in hard practice during the journey, constantly exceeding the scheduled practice time several times over, in order to give the people of all countries in the world a great stimulus at the spiritual mountain meeting and to show China's inherent martial spirit. After the ship leaves Hong Kong, all the team members will organize a entertainment show to be held in the ship's music hall. On the eve of arrival in Singapore, there will be a grand occasion. The voyage is expected to arrive in Singapore on the morning of the 2nd.

On Board the Conte Verde, En Route from Shanghai to Hong Kong, Sent by Yi Qin, Newspaper Correspondent Accompanying the Delegation

Special Report from This Newspaper: The Chinese World Games delegation, consisting of more than 110 people, boarded the Italian mail ship Conte Verde at noon on June 26. After saying goodbye to the well-wishers from various groups at the Zhaoshang Wharf amidst enthusiastic cheers, the journey was smooth and the weather was sunny and refreshing. At 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 28th, they safely arrived in Hong Kong. The life at sea of the delegation members attending the World Games on behalf of our country is full of interest and must be of concern to the people of the country. Therefore, I have to write it down.

After boarding the ship, the team members ran around looking for their cabins. Because the staff members lived in second-class cabins, and the athletes and inspection team members lived in second-class economy cabins, they were separated from each other, which was very inconvenient. Therefore, many athletes could not enter through the same door after boarding the ship, which was also an interesting thing.

The food on the ship is Italian style. Although it is not particularly good, it is still rich and edible. Each day is divided into three meals: breakfast, lunch, and dinner, as well as a tea break. The team members slept comfortably and ate well, so there is a tendency to become fat, which is indeed a major problem.

At 5:00 PM on the 27th, a plenary meeting of the delegation was held in the first-class cabin's music room. Shen Siliang chaired the meeting and reported on the expectations for this trip abroad. He urged all team members not to neglect small personal matters because personal actions represent the group. Therefore, every word and action must be paid attention to in order to show an organized performance to outsiders. If there are any unsatisfactory matters, opinions can be submitted to the team managers, and private discussions should be avoided. Everyone must unite sincerely and hope that those with problems regarding their professional qualifications will honestly report themselves to avoid being pointed out by people from other countries, which would damage the national image.

Various committees were established to manage life at sea. There are four types:

Training Committee: Ma Yuehan (Chairman), Dong Shouyi, Xu Minhui, Hao Ming, Ye Liang (regarding athletes' practice, etc.)

Speech Committee: Yuan Dunli (Chairman), Gao Zi, Wu Wei (regarding discussions on German and Western etiquette, etc.)

Entertainment Committee: Dong Shouyi (Chairman), Wu Bangwei, Zhao Wenzao, Qian Yiqin, Wang Huaiqi, Huang Liming, Shao Rugan (regarding entertainment and social events for the entire delegation, etc.)

Management Committee: Zhou Jiaqi (Chairman), Shi Zhaokang, Shen Kunnan, Song Junfu, Li Youzhen, Li Qingan, Gu Shunhua (regarding all matters related to the delegation's affairs)

Starting from the second day (27th), a small number of athletes have begun to practice on the deck. Weightlifting representatives Huang Sheji, Shen Liang, Weng Kangting, and Zhai Lianyuan (national arts) and Li Sen are the most active. In addition to practicing, most of the other athletes play chess to entertain themselves. Among the team members, only Xu Yingchao suffered from seasickness, and Jiang Lianggui was unwell due to a cold. The rest were full of energy as usual.

Daughter's Matchmaker

Grand Shanghai Screens Romeo and Juliet 158

Lai

Starring Norma Shearer and Leslie Howard 159

John Barrymore Takes a Supporting Role in This Film 160

Now, the reason why the adaptation of Shakespeare's works to the screen, such as the performance of "A Midsummer Night's Dream," has gained unprecedented audiences in the world is not without reason. Last winter, the Soviet Union held a "Shakespeare Congress," and the United States also has an organization for the Shakespeare Annual Meeting. "Romeo and Juliet" is a very popular reading material in the world. MGM plans to put it on the screen, which has been a long time. It was decided that Norma Shearer would be the female lead. At first, it was intended to be shelved because a suitable actor for the male lead could not be found. However, MGM, seeing the success of Warner's "A Midsummer Night's Dream," revived the old plan. Now, MGM has selected Leslie Howard as the male lead, which has been agreed upon by Ms. Shearer, and John Barrymore has taken a supporting role in this film. Its future success is expected to exceed "A Midsummer Night's Dream."

Formerly a Waiter at a Dance Hall: Ding Zhenglin Attempts to Rob a Russian and is Arrested; Remaining Thieves Flee Without a Trace; Yesterday Handed Over to the Court for Trial 161

A Russian man,羅巴司道夫 (transliterated), residing at No. 16,培納 Apartments, at the intersection of呂班 Road and麥賽而蒂羅 Road in the French Concession, was suddenly attacked by three Chinese bandits armed with guns at around 6 a.m. the day before yesterday. The bandits broke open the door and rushed in, attempting to rob him. The Russian man, awakened by the noise, discovered that one of the three bandits was Ding Zhenglin, a former waiter from Zhenjiang (age 37) whom he had previously employed. He forcefully subdued Ding and pushed him out of the room, causing a collision with the other two bandits. Seeing that their attempt had failed, the two bandits fled in different directions. However, the bandit with the handgun fired two shots at the wall as a warning. Fortunately, no one was injured. The doorman numbered 491, hired by the apartment building, and police patrolman number 289 from the French police station, hearing the commotion, arrived and arrested Ding. Detective Zhou Bingcheng and investigators Qin Youyu and Wu Wengang interrogated him. According to Ding's confession, he had worked as a waiter at a dance hall at the intersection of馬斯南 Road and震飛 Road. After quitting, he was unemployed. On the night of the 28th of last month, he met a friend, Zhang Faqing, at the Great World amusement park, who invited him to stay at Zhang's house at No. 753民國 Road. There, they planned the robbery. After reaching a decision, Zhang, carrying a handgun, invited an unknown person, and Ding led them to his former employer's house to attempt the robbery. He claimed that Zhang and the other unknown person had fled and he did not know their whereabouts. Yesterday at noon, he was sent to the Special No. 2 Court, Criminal Division 1. Police Department lawyer Chen Ming presented the case, requesting a postponement of the trial because the investigation was not yet complete. Judge Li Changnian reviewed the report, questioned Ding, and ordered a postponement until the 15th to further investigate. The defendant was returned to custody.

A Rogue Demands Money and Takes Someone to the Authorities 162

Wu Fengxin, a 24-year-old local resident who deals in foreign goods and lives at No. 13露杳園 Road, was sipping tea on the third floor of a teahouse in the邑廟裏園 (City God Temple Garden) a few days ago when he was inexplicably accosted by a rogue named Gu Jiubao, who gathered several hooligans to extort money from Wu. Gu falsely accused Wu of owing gambling debts. Wu denied the accusation, stating that he did not know Gu. Consequently, Gu and his gang brutally beat and injured Wu. Since he was alone and outnumbered and under surveillance, a member of Gu's gang mediated, and the matter was settled for 69 yuan. Wu paid 19 yuan in cash on the spot and wrote an IOU for the remaining 50 yuan, promising to pay it back within a month. Wu then managed to escape home and sought medical treatment for his injuries. Feeling aggrieved, he filed a report with the邑廟 police station, requesting a thorough investigation and the return of the extorted money. Police Chief Yu summoned Gu Jiubao for questioning yesterday. Gu confessed that he operated a雀牌 (mahjong) parlor. In August of last year, a salesman named Xu Sheng from his parlor sold 26 sets of雀牌 to Wu Fengxin, a purchasing agent at the運勝 foreign firm, for a total of 138 yuan. He had not received any payment. Unexpectedly, the運勝 foreign firm closed down in less than a month. Recently, he happened to see Wu Fengxin in the裏園 and demanded the debt be repaid, which was then mediated. He denied any extortion or assault. The case involves public disturbance and assault causing injury and was transferred to the General Bureau for handling.

Jin Pengling Bravely Fights Off Petty Thieves, Captures One, and Discovers the Wooden Fake Handgun; Zhang Azhong Handed Over to the Detective Squad 163

Yesterday at around 11 a.m., four thieves dressed in formal attire, pretending to ask for a letter, broke into the home of Jin Pengling, a Land Bureau employee. They displayed handguns, demanding silence, and began beating Jin and his family, demanding they hand over silver dollars. However, Jin was not intimidated. Seeing that the guns were made of wood, he disregarded them and resisted the thieves. The thieves panicked and, not daring to search the house, fled in a hurry. Jin chased after them. Two of the thieves turned back and pretended to shoot. Jin rushed forward to tackle them and was struck on the right forehead with the fake handgun, causing profuse bleeding. At that moment, police officer Zhang Yuting and others from the文廟 Road post, having heard the alarm, arrived one after another. With the help of passersby, they apprehended one of the thieves, who was wearing a white silk long gown, and seized a fake handgun. Another fake handgun was also recovered on the road. The thief and the two guns were taken to the police station. After questioning by Chief Wen, the thief was identified as Zhang Azhong (age 30). He was handed over to the detective squad for further investigation and to apprehend the remaining gang members. The victim, Jin, was bleeding from his injuries and was sent to a nearby hospital for treatment by another officer.

Jiang Wanzhen's Teacher, Zhang Ziliang, Dies After Jumping From a Building and Breaking Bones 164

Zhang Ziliang, a Suzhou native and the teacher of the famous female蘇灘 performer Jiang Wanzhen, was already in his sixties and lacked any means of support. He relied on his student Wanzhen for his daily living. However, on the 27th of last month, Jiang's father, concerned that Zhang was old and frail and might encounter unforeseen circumstances, sent him to the home of Zhang's son-in-law, Jiang Rongqing, at No. 31寶裕坊,成都 Road. Although Zhang was unwilling, he had no choice and could only lament his fate. Unexpectedly, on the 29th, due to this resentment, he suddenly jumped from the window of the front building, committing suicide. He was severely injured in the fall. His son-in-law and others quickly noticed and summoned an ambulance, which rushed him to the hospital. However, medical treatment was ineffective, and he died yesterday morning. The hospital reported the incident to the Chengdu Road police station in the jurisdiction, who ordered detective Zhang Peilan to investigate. The body was then taken to the斐倫 Road morgue for an autopsy. At around 10 a.m., Prosecutor Zhang Zongru, appointed by the First Special District Local Court, arrived to examine the body. After华捕头 (Chinese constable) Jiang Linxiang reported the results of the investigation, Zhang ruled that the deceased, Zhang Ziliang, was male and had died from broken bones sustained during a fall from a building. The body was released to his son-in-law, Jiang Rongqing, for burial after he signed a guarantee.

A Group of Robbers Sentenced to Prison; Eleven Guilty in Five Robbery Cases 165

The homes of Wu Xu氏 at No. 6西華德 Road, Zhang Zicong at No. 435小沙渡 Road, Gao Yuan氏 at No. 6平凉 Road, Chen Xiulin at No. 80東百老匯 Road, and Wo Yang氏 at No. 29東有恒 Road were invaded by multiple robbers between March 5th and April 28th of this year. The robbers brandished handguns, demanded silence, and stole valuables worth over 1,000 yuan before fleeing. The victims reported the incidents to the police station, requesting their apprehension. Subsequently, the Hongkou and Jing'an Temple police stations and special agencies, including Chinese detectives Yue Huayoushan, Jin Haibo, Chen Dabao, Xie Futang, Zhao Fuhai, Hu Guangrong, Qian Xianting, and Lü Shouchang, arrested the main robbers, Lu A'er, Liu Fugen, Gu Xiaohu, Peng Renjie, Yuan Youqiao, and the suspect Qin Huasheng, along with twenty-one women. Three handguns and thirteen bullets were seized. They were successively sent to the Special No. 1 Court. Except for Qin Huasheng and the woman Miao Hong氏, and six other people, who were released after being found to be not involved, the remaining robbers were interrogated and awaited sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao XieFen presided over the Criminal Division 3 court and sentenced Lu A'er, Liu Fugen, Wang Guifu, and Peng Renjie to seven years of imprisonment each, Qiu Jiyu to six years, Jiang Ruiqing to five years, Zhang Yikang, Wang Xiaosan, and Gu Xiaohu to four years each, Yuan Youqiao to three years, and Zhang Shilin to two years. The guns and bullets were confiscated. Fei A'quan and Peng Chen氏 were acquitted and released with a reprimand.

Two Drug Cases, One Sentenced, One Postponed 166

Opium

Chinese constable No. 1365 and Sino-Western detectives arrested Wang Gengsheng, a Chongming native, at around 9 p.m. the night before last on the No. 10 public bus near the intersection of East-West華德 Road and兆豐 Road. They found two packages of opium on his person, weighing one and a half taels. He confessed that he had bought it from Wang Jin氏, a Jiaxing woman at No. 9新閘 Road. The detectives rushed to the address and arrested her, seizing sixteen packages of opium, large and small, weighing nine taels in total, as well as a set of opium-smoking paraphernalia and approximately ten yuan in silver dollars and copper coins. They were taken to the匯山 police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Criminal Division 3 of the Special No. 1 Court. After Judge Xiao questioned the two defendants, Wang Jin氏 was sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment, and Wang Gengsheng was fined thirty yuan. The evidence was confiscated.

Heroin

Chinese detective Cui Chengke from the匯山 police station arrested Liu Baosheng, a Shandong native selling heroin, near the intersection of東有恒 Road and公平 Road at around 1 p.m. the day before yesterday. A small packet of heroin was found on his person. He claimed to live at No. 52三官堂,華記 Road, and that his father had asked him to deliver it to a Mr. Yang at No. 980東有恒 Road. Detective Cui and Liu went to the address to arrest Yang, but he was not found. They then went to Liu's home, where they found a Tongzhou woman, Chen Yan氏, sleeping in the亭子間 (maid's room). Three more packets of the same drug were found under the bed and in a bamboo basket. Chen was arrested and taken to the police station along with Liu and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Criminal Division 3 of the Special No. 1 Court.工部局 (Municipal Council) lawyer Zhang Shizhu requested a postponement. Detective Cui then presented the evidence and explained the details of the case. When questioned, the two defendants gave evasive answers. Judge Xiao ordered them to be detained and postponed the case for further review.

How Many Unidentified Male Corpses? 167

In front of the仁德會 gate on淞興 Road,吳淞, a male corpse was found on the road yesterday morning. The deceased was around 40 years old, wearing a black diagonal-纹短衫袴 (short jacket and trousers), with a trouser belt wrapped around his neck three times. The police station ordered the保甲 (local warden) Zhou Lansheng to report it to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Li Fen and coroner Shen Qixiu were appointed to the scene to examine the corpse, determining that the deceased had been strangled to death before death. The論由堂 (charitable organization) took custody of the body for burial, awaiting investigation and apprehension of the murderer.

A nameless male corpse was discovered in the Suzhou Creek inside the新橋 of the閘北舢板廠 (sampan factory) yesterday morning. The deceased was around 30 years old, wearing a blue cloth short jacket, black cloth trousers, yellow socks, and no shoes. The山水巡隊 (canal patrol) discovered the corpse, seized it, and ordered the 保甲 (local warden) Shen Xiaohe, of the 11th圖 of the 27th保, to report it to the local court for an autopsy. Shanghai Universal Goodness Villa June Charity Report 169

In June of the 25th year of the Republic (1936), the Shanghai Universal Goodness Villa collected and buried 154 large coffins, 2,815 small coffins, and 30 sets of bones in the Northern and Southern Chinese Concessions. It provided 1,273 large and small coffins. This included 14 large coffins, 1,587 small coffins, and 20 sets of bones collected by the main villa. The 斜桥 (Xieqiao) and 南市 (Nanshi) branch villas and various charitable halls in the French Concession collected 604 small coffins. The Public Concession police stations and the Health Bureau notified the collection of abandoned infant corpses and unclaimed bodies from the morgue and various hospitals within the concession, including 127 large coffins and 577 small coffins. The Health Bureau notified the burial of floating coffins in滬西 (West Shanghai) and 閘北 (Zhabei), including 叫 (call) large coffins and 28 small coffins, and 10 sets of bones. The 聯義善會 (United Righteous Charity Association) collected 14 small coffins. The Chinese Women and Children Relief Society Orphanage collected 3 large coffins. The Red Cross First Hospital collected 2 large coffins. The惠旅 (Hui Lü) Hospital collected 1 large coffin. The Shanghai Epidemic Hospital collected 1 large coffin. The辛未 (Xinwei) Relief Society collected 1 large coffin. The Chinese Leprosy Hospital collected 1 large coffin. The平民療養院 (People's Sanatorium) collected 1 small coffin. The Shanghai Sanatorium collected 2 small coffins. The慈航 (Ci Hang) Hospital collected 2 small coffins. All of the above corpses were collected by the villa and transported to the Yi Di (cemetery) in the Da Chang Tang Qiao area for burial and marked for later identification. In addition, the White Cross Universal Goodness Obstetrics and Gynecology Hospital on Xinmin Road, Zhabei, provided 3,539 diagnoses and prescriptions.

Changshu Guild Rescues Yao Shiquan; Submits Petition to Headquarters for Lenient Treatment; Authorities Clearly Investigate and Reduce Sentence 170

According to the Great Public Society, Yao Shiquan, a member of the Changshu Guild and a rice merchant, was deceived by Zhu Shulin, who operated an opium den on the South Wharf, and falsely named as the owner of the opium den. He was arrested by the Municipal Public Security Bureau and transferred to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for legal action. After Yao Shiquan's family came to Shanghai and reported the matter to the Guild, the Guild prepared a document and submitted it to the Garrison Headquarters, requesting lenient treatment. It was explained that Yao Shiquan was deceived by Song Shulin and falsely named, and according to the law, he should be sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined. Fortunately, after the Guild's best efforts to rescue him, his sentence was reduced to three months of imprisonment, and the fine was also waived. He is expected to be released within the next month. It is also heard that the Guild will report the details of the extortion of Yao Shiquan by vagrants to the competent authorities for strict investigation and punishment.

Omitted. 11. Regarding the letter from Gu Yuncheng requesting the association to mediate the inheritance dispute of his deceased father, Zi Xia Gong. Central Restaurant Opens Today 172

The former Central Western Restaurant at No. 730 Fuzhou Road has now been reorganized as the Central Hotel. It has been completely renovated and a large sum of money has been spent on installing the latest air conditioning system, with a suitable temperature. It is also economical and hygienic, making it a leading modernized standard hotel in Shanghai. It is said that the shareholders of the hotel are all well-known figures in Shanghai, such as Du Yuesheng and Jin Jiulin, as well as famous lawyers Wu Peng and Yu Hualong. It is understood that the opening ceremony will be held by Yuan Ludeng this morning. It is certain that it will be filled with guests and be a lively event.

Barbers' Guild Holds Second Re-election Convention the Day Before Yesterday 173

The Shanghai Barbers' Guild has been established in June of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). It has been two years now. It was reported that the second re-election convention was held at the guild hall at No. 1 Tongde Lane, Xieqiao, Nanshi, at 4 p.m. the day before yesterday. Although the weather was hot, the members were very enthusiastic. All members, including Zhou Hongde, Li Yongcheng, Tang Yushan, Zhu Mingqing, Gong Dawei, Qian Shouling, Chen Yongting, and Wang Chunbo, attended, as well as representatives from the Social Bureau, Zhang Dafu, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Yuan Hongjun, and over one hundred guests from the Municipal Party Department. Yu Wanquan, Zhu Mingqing, Xia Mingqing, Xin Yuling, and Zhang Yujin were publicly elected as the presidium of the convention. Tang Huaxuan served as the master of ceremonies, and Pan Xiyang and Wang Erjun served as the recorders. The chairman reported, briefly stating, "Today is the date for the second re-election of the executive and supervisory committee members of the guild. I am very impressed that all the members are enthusiastically participating in this hot weather. Our guild has been established for two years now. The affairs of the guild have gone through many difficulties in these two years, which I think all the members are aware of. However, there are more than 2,000 barber shops in the city, and most have joined the guild, but many have not yet joined. I hope that everyone will work hard to take responsibility from now on, take practical action, and unite in spirit, so that our guild will develop daily. This is what I hope for very much." Representatives from the party and government agencies then delivered speeches (the speeches are omitted). Guests and members also delivered speeches in succession. Then, the re-election of the executive and supervisory committee members began. Representatives from the Municipal Party Department, Social Bureau, and Municipal Chamber of Commerce supervised the counting of the ballots. Zhu Mingqing, Xia Mingqing, Jin Wanquan, Chen Yongting Wang Chunbo, Li Yongcheng, and Xue Guangdian were elected as the seven executive members. Hu Yucai and Zheng Renheng were elected as alternate executive members. Zhang Yujin, Wang Guobao, and Chen Shengxi were elected as the two supervisory committee members. Zhu Yucheng was elected as an alternate supervisory member. The new officers were scheduled to be sworn into office on July 16th at 2 p.m., and all city representatives were welcome to attend the ceremony. Representatives Zhou Hongde, Xin Yuling, and Xia Mingqing also proposed three motions: Submit a request to the Aviation Association to approve the collection of aviation national salvation donations from the barber industry; Establish the Shanghai Barber Industry New Life Labor Service Corps; Change the membership procedures of the guild: (A) Basic members: those who have already joined will start collecting monthly fees from today; (B) Special members: those who have not yet joined only need to participate enthusiastically and will not be charged a membership fee for the time being, but will first pay the monthly fee; (D) Ordinary members: barber shops in the border areas can participate voluntarily. All three motions were unanimously approved by the city representatives. The meeting adjourned.

English expert Ge Lejun (Ge Chuanqiao) began giving public lectures on various difficult questions concerning English pronunciation and other topics at the Sichuan Road YMCA the day before yesterday (it is said that the lectures will be held from July 1st to 6th, from 7:30 p.m. to 9 p.m. each night).
